Question:
“What’s your programme after the examination?” asked Hira. Mira said, “I’ve not decided. Can you suggest any?” “Let us go on a picnic,” said Hira. “What an excellent idea it is!” said Mira.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Hira asked Mira what her (M) programme was after the examination. Míra replied that she (M) had not decided and asked Hira if she (H) could suggest any. In response, Hira proposed that they should go on a picnic. Mira then exclaimed with joy that it was an excellent idea.

Explanation:
Explanation: The direct exclamation "What an excellent idea it is!" is reported by changing the exclamatory form into a statement: "that it was an excellent idea." We also change the tense (present to past) and use a reporting verb that shows exclamation, so "said" becomes "exclaimed." Therefore the correct reported form is "Mira exclaimed that it was an excellent idea."

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Mrs. Nasima said to her student, "I heard the news of your illness yesterday. How are you now?" "I feel a bit well today, madam," replied the student. "Don't worry. You will come round soon," said Mrs. Nasima.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
When reporting speech we backshift tenses and change time words: "I heard" → "had heard", "yesterday" → "the previous day", and "How are you now?" → "how she was then". Also the student's line is more natural as "she felt a bit better that day" (not "a bit well"), and "You will come round soon" becomes "she would come round soon" to match the past reporting verb.

Question #131 (ID: 481562)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“Good morning, students,” said the teacher. “How are you?” “We are fine, sir. What about you?” “I am fine too. Please, sit down.” “Have you prepared your lesson?” the teacher asked. “Sorry, sir, we have not prepared our lesson,” they replied.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The teacher wished the students good morning and asked them how they were. The students respectfully replied that they were fine and asked the teacher how he was. The teacher replied that he was fine too and told them to sit down. Then he asked them if they had prepared their lesson. They sorrowfully/sadly replied with respect that they had not prepared their lesson.

Explanation:
This is direct speech converted to reported speech, so the reporting verbs (said, asked, replied) are past and we shift tenses back: e.g., “We are fine” becomes “they said they were fine,” and “Have you prepared your lesson?” becomes “he asked them if they had prepared their lesson.” Pronouns and possessives also change (we → they, our → their) to match the new speaker and subject.

Question #132 (ID: 481563)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“Have you ever been to Cox’s Bazar?” asked Shahab. “No, I have never,” replied Labib. “But I desire for visiting the place.” “I had an opportunity to visit the sea-beach last year,” said Shabab. “Let us go there this week,” said Labib.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Shabab asked Labib if (whether) he (L) had ever been to Cox's Bazar. Labib replied in the negative and said that he had never been (gone) there. But he said that he desired for visiting the place. Shabab said that he had an opportunity to visit the seabeach the previous year. Labib proposed to Shabab that they should (might) go there that week

Explanation:
When converting to reported speech, tenses and time expressions shift back: present perfect ([math]have/has + past participle[/math]) becomes past perfect ([math]had + past participle[/math]), "this/last" become "that/the previous" and imperatives/suggestions become reported suggestions. So Shahab’s question becomes "Shahab asked if he had ever been to Cox’s Bazar," Labib’s "No, I have never" becomes "Labib replied that he had never been," Shabab’s past comment stays past perfect ("he had had an opportunity… the previous year"), and "Let us go there this week" becomes "Labib suggested going there that week."

Question #133 (ID: 481564)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“Konika, have you done your English lesson today?” asked the teacher. “Yes, sir,” she replied. “But I have not understood one gramatical point.” The teacher assured her saying, “Come to my room. I will help you understand the point.” “Thank you, sir,” she smilingly said.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The teacher asked Konica if she had done her English lesson that day. She respectfully replied in the affirmative and said that she had not understood one grammatical point. The teacher assured her telling her to go to his room. He again said that he would help her understand the point. She smilingly thanked him respectfully.

Explanation:
Explanation: The word "gramatical" is a spelling error; it should be "grammatical." "Smilingly" is not a standard adverb in this context; use the participial form or phrase—e.g. "she said, smiling" or "she said with a smile." Also place a comma before the participial phrase ("The teacher assured her, saying…") to separate it from the main clause.

Question:
The teacher said to the girl, “Do you think that honesty is the best policy?” The girl said, “Yes, sir, I think so.” “Then learn to be honest from your childhood,” said the teacher. “Thank you, sir,” said the girl. “May Allah bless you,” said the teacher.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The teacher asked the girl if she thought that honesty is the best policy. The girl respectfully replied in the affirmative and said that she thought so. Then the teacher advised her (s) to learn to be honest from her childhood. The girl respectfully thanked him (t). The teacher prayed that Allah might bless her.

Explanation:
The correct answer identifies the teacher’s sentence “Then learn to be honest from your childhood” as advice (an imperative) given after the girl agreed that honesty is best. The dialogue shows speech functions in order—question (opinion), agreement, advice, gratitude, and a blessing—so recognizing the imperative/advice is why that option is right.

Question #135 (ID: 481566)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
The girl said to the teacher, “Sir, I shall be grateful if you kindly lend me the book you praised highly in the classroom yesterday.” The teacher said, “I have become really happy to know that you are eager to read this book. You are welcome to any of my books that you like.” “Thank you, sir,” said the girl. “You are welcome,” said the teacher.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Addressing him as sir, the girl respectfully told the teacher that she would be grateful if he kindly lent her the book he had praised highly in the classroom the previous day. The teacher said that he had become really happy to know that she was eager to read that book. He added that she was welcome to any of his books that she liked. The girl thanked him politely. Then the teacher told her that she was welcome.

Explanation:
When reported, pronouns, verb tenses and time words change: the girl’s “I shall be grateful if you kindly lend me the book you praised highly in the classroom yesterday” becomes “She said (that) she would be grateful if he lent her the book he had praised in the classroom the previous day,” because [math]\text{shall}\to\text{would}[/math], “you” → “he”, and “yesterday” → “the previous day.” The teacher’s reply becomes “He said he was very pleased to know she was eager to read it and that she was welcome to any of his books she liked,” following the same pronoun and tense shifts; finally “Thank you” → “she thanked him” and “You are welcome” → “he replied that she was welcome.” These changes follow the rules of sequence of tenses and shifting references in indirect speech.

Question #136 (ID: 481567)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Once a rich banker said to a poor cobbler, "How much do you earn a year?" The cobbler replied laughing, "I never count in this way. I earn barely enough to pass a day. And I'm happy." "Are you really happy?" said the banker.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Once a rich banker asked a poor cobbler how much he (c) earned a year. The cobbler replied laughing that he (c) never counted in that way. He (c) also added that he (c) earned barely enough to pass a day and he (c) was happy. Then the banker asked him (c) if he (c) was really happy.

Explanation:
The cobbler is right because he measures happiness by having enough each day and feeling content, not by comparing large sums of money; this shows happiness is subjective and comes from meeting needs and expectations. The banker’s view wrongly ties happiness to wealth, illustrating that more money doesn't automatically create greater well‑being.

Question #137 (ID: 481568)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
The teacher said to the student, "Have you prepared your lesson today?" "No, sir," replied the student. The teacher said. "Why?" "I was suffering from headache yesterday. I shall do my work tomorrow," said the student.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The teacher asked the student if he (s) had prepared his lesson that day. The student respectfully replied in the negative and said that he hadn't. The teacher asked again why he (s) had not prepared his lesson. The student replied that he (s) had been suffering from headache the previous day. He (s) added that he (s) would do his (s) work the next day.

Explanation:
In reported speech the tense shifts back because the reporting verb is in the past: "Have you prepared your lesson today?" becomes "he asked if he had prepared his lesson that day" (present perfect → past perfect, "today" → "that day"). "I was suffering from headache yesterday" becomes "he said he had been suffering from a headache the day before" (past continuous → past perfect continuous, "yesterday" → "the day before"). "I shall do my work tomorrow" becomes "he said he would do his work the next day" ("shall" → "would", "tomorrow" → "the next day").

Question:
“Good morning, students,” said the teacher. “How are you?” “We are fine, sir. What about you?” “I am fine too. Please, sit down.” “Have you prepared your lesson?” the teacher asked. “Sorry, sir, we have not prepared our lesson,” they replied.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
এখানে সরাসরি কথাকে পরোক্ষ কথায় রূপান্তরের নিয়মগুলো প্রয়োগ করা হয়েছে: বর্তমান কাল অতীত কালে সরানো হয়েছে, বক্তার সর্বনাম (we → they) বদলানো হয়েছে, এবং প্রশ্ন ও অনুরোধকে উপযুক্ত রূপে (প্রশ্নে “how/if” যোগ করে, অনুরোধে “requested/told” ব্যবহার করে) রিপোর্ট করা হয়েছে। উদাহরণস্বরুপ “How are you?” → অনুরোধকারীকে “asked how they were”, “We are fine” → “they said they were fine”, “Have you prepared your lesson?” → “asked if/whether they had prepared their lesson”, “Please, sit down.” → “requested them to sit down” করা হয়েছে। এই নিয়মগুলোর কারণেই পরোক্ষ ভাষ্যের সঠিক উত্তরসমূহ এসব রূপে দেওয়া হয়েছে।

Question:
“May I come in, sir?” Ripon said to his class teacher. The teacher replied, “Yes, why are you so late today?” “My grandfather suddenly felt severe pain in his chest. So, I rushed to hospital with him.” “May Allah grant his quick recovery,” said the teacher.

Solution:


Explanation:
The teacher’s reply is a polite expression of sympathy and a prayer for the grandfather’s speedy recovery, which is an appropriate response to hearing about someone’s sudden illness. It shows concern and offers comfort, making it the natural and correct reaction in that situation.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
All answers come directly from the speakers’ lines: the lady says “To Rajshahi” (destination), “Three first class tickets” (number = three and class = first class), and the officer says “they will cost you three thousands taka” (price). In dialogue questions, match each question word to the corresponding part of the reply—"where" → place, "how many" → number, "which class" → type/class, "how much" → cost—so you extract the required facts.

“Why are you laughing in the class?” the teacher said to the girl. “I have remembered interesting incident after you have given the example.” “What is that?” said the teacher. “It is about one of my cousins who came to our house yesterday.” “Forget it and be attentive to your lesson.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:

Question #144 (ID: 481575)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board

Question:
Rina said to Sima, “Why don’t you get up early from sleep?” Sima said, “It is tough for me to leave bed early.” “Alas! It is a bad habit,” said Rina, “If you leave bed early, you can enjoy sound health. Follow my advice.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
In reported speech we backshift tenses and change pronouns: Rina’s question becomes, “Rina asked Sima why she did not get up early,” and Sima’s reply becomes, “she said that it was difficult for her to get up early.” Exclamations and advice are turned into statements or verbs of saying—“Alas! It is a bad habit” becomes a regretful remark in past tense, the conditional “If you leave… you can enjoy…” shifts to “if she got up early she could enjoy…,” and “Follow my advice” becomes “advised her to follow her advice.”

Question #145 (ID: 481576)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“Good morning, Kiron,” said Harun. “How much preparation have you taken for the SSC Examination?” “A great preparation,” Kiron replied. “Wow! What an intelligent boy!” said Harun. “May you be distinguished with your result.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
অপ্রত্যক্ষ বাক্যে সরাসরি কথ্য রূপান্তরের সময় কাল পিছিয়ে দেওয়া (present perfect → past perfect), সর্বনাম পরিবর্তন ও প্রশ্ন-উক্তিকে তথ্যবাচক বাক্যে রূপান্তর করা দরকার; তাই "How much preparation have you taken?" হয় "asked him how much preparation he had taken।" "A great preparation" অনূদিত হলে বলা হবে "he said he had done a great deal of preparation", "What an intelligent boy!" হয় "Harun praised him as an intelligent boy" এবং "May you be distinguished with your result" হয় "Harun wished him that he might be distinguished by his result"—এই নিয়মগুলো মেনে অনুবাদ সঠিক।

Question #146 (ID: 481577)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Let’s have a walk outside the farm, —?

(b) I am in the habit of walking every morning, —?

(c) Morning entertains us with fresh air, —?

(d) No one should miss the opportunity, —?

(e) Have a try to form this habit of morning walk, —?

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
ক উত্তর: "shall we?" — কারণ "Let's..." বাক্যে আমরা নিজেরাও যোগদানে বলছি, তাই ট্যাগ প্রশ্নে "shall we?" ব্যবহার করা হয়।

খ উত্তর: "aren't I?" — কারণ সাধারণভাবে "I am" থাকা ট্যাগ প্রশ্নে আম-বাক্যের জন্য অপ্রচলিত "amn't I" নয়, বরং স্বাভাবিকভাবে "aren't I?" বলা হয় (বা সৌজন্যভাবে "am I not?")।

গ উত্তর: "doesn't it?" — কারণ "Morning" তৃতীয় পুরুষ একবচন, present simple দিয়ে হয়েছে; ট্যাগে সহায়ক ক্রিয়া "does" নেগেটিভ করে "doesn't it?" হয়।

ঘ উত্তর: "should they?" — কারণ "No one" একবচন ব্যক্তি নির্দেশ করে কিন্তু নেতিবাচক অর্থ রয়েছে, তাই ট্যাগে ইতিবাচক সাহায্যকারী ব্যবহার করে "should they?" বলা হয়।

ঙ উত্তর: "will you?" — কারণ এটি অনুরোধ/আজ্ঞা ধাঁচের বাক্য; এমন ইম্পেরেটিভ বাক্যে সাধারণ ট্যাগ হলো "will you?" (অথবা বেশি শিষ্টভাবে "would you?")।

“Please give me your English Grammar And Composition Book,” said Sara. ‘I cannot give,” said Niha. “I have to take it with me in the class.”  “I shall return the book before the class starts,” said Sara. “Take it,” said Niha. “Thank you,” said Sara.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:

Question #155 (ID: 481586)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2018 | Boards:  | Tags: All Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Shabab said to Tahsin, “Did you visit the Shat Gombuj Mosque?” “No, I didn’t,” said Tahsin. “I visited there last week. How beautiful the mosque is!” said Shahab. “Let’s go there next year,” Tahsin said.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Shabab asked Tahsin if he (T) had visited the Shat Gambuj Mosque. Tahsin replied in the negative saying that he (T) hadn't visited the Shat Gambuj Mosque. Then Shabab said that he (S) had been there the previous week. He then exclaimed in wonder that the mosque was very beautiful. After that Tahsin proposed that they should go there the following year.

Explanation:
Explanation: In reported speech the past simple question "Did you visit...?" becomes past perfect, so it becomes "Shabab asked Tahsin if he had visited the Shat Gombuj Mosque." Negative reply "No, I didn't" is reported as "he said he hadn't." Shahab's "I visited there last week" becomes "he said he had visited it the previous week," and the exclamation "How beautiful the mosque is!" becomes "how beautiful the mosque was." "Let's go there next year" is a suggestion, reported as "Tahsin suggested they should go there the following year" or "Tahsin said they would go there the following year."

Question #156 (ID: 481587)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2018 | Boards:  | Tags: All Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Shabab said to Tahsin, “Did you visit the Shat Gombuj Mosque?” “No, I didn’t,” said Tahsin. “I visited there last week. How beautiful the mosque is!” said Shahab. “Let’s go there next year,” Tahsin said.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
In reported speech we backshift tenses and turn questions into reported yes/no questions with if/whether, so Shabab’s “Did you visit the Shat Gombuj Mosque?” becomes “Shabab asked Tahsin if he had visited the Shat Gombuj Mosque.”  
Negatives and time words change accordingly: “No, I didn’t” → “he said he hadn’t,” and “last week” → “the previous week”; exclamations use verbs like “exclaimed” and tense shift: “How beautiful the mosque is!” → “he exclaimed how beautiful the mosque was.”  
Suggestions are reported with verbs like “suggested” plus a gerund and time change: “Let’s go there next year” → “Tahsin suggested going there the following year.”

Question #157 (ID: 481588)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
My mother said, “Won’t you go to school today?” I said, “Mother, I feel feverish today. I don’t want to go to school.” “Ok, take a rest now. You should be more careful about your health,” said mother.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
My mother asked me if I would not go to school that day. In reply, I told mother that I felt feverish that day and so I didn't want to go to school. Mother said that it was alright and advised me to take rest then. She further told me that I should be more careful about my health.

Explanation:
এখানে সরাসরি বক্তব্যকে পরোক্ষ (reported) কথায় বদলে বলার নিয়ম অনুসরণ করা হয়েছে: প্রশ্নকে "asked" দিয়ে এবং "Won't you..." থেকে সময় ও কালের পরিবর্তন করে "if I would go to school that day" বলা হয়, প্রথম পুরুষ/প্রথম-পর্দায়কের পরিবর্তে উপযুক্ত সর্বনাম বদলে নেওয়া হয়েছে, এবং "today/now" → "that day/then" ও বর্তমান কাল → অতীত কালে পরিবর্তন করা হয়েছে; similarly নির্দেশ/পরামর্শকে "told" বা "advised" দিয়ে পরোক্ষভাবে প্রকাশ করা হয়েছে। এই পরিবর্তনগুলোই ঠিক উত্তরকে সঠিক করে কারণ এগুলোই reported speech-এর মৌলিক নিয়ম।

Question #158 (ID: 481589)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“Good morning, can I help you?” said the manager. “Yes, I was told to come over here to get a parking sticker. Is it the right place? “said the lady. “Yes, it is. What’s the registration number of your car? ” said the manager.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The manager wished the lady good morning and asked her if he could help her. The lady replied in the affirmative and said that she had been told to go over there to get a parking sticker. Out of curiosity, she again asked the manager if that was the right place. Then the manager replied in the affirmative and said that it was the right place and at the same time asked the lady what the registration number of her car was.

Explanation:
In reported speech, direct questions use “asked if/whether” and verbs shift back in time (for example, “can” → “could”, “is” → “was”, “was told” → “had been told”) and pronouns are changed as needed. So the correct indirect version uses these changes: the manager asked if he could help, the lady said she had been told to come for a parking sticker and asked if that was the right place, and the manager replied that it was and asked what the registration number of her car was.

Question:
“My sons, listen to me. A great treasure lies hidden in the land. I am going to leave it to you.” “How will we find it?” said the sons. “You must dig the land for it,” said the old man.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The old man ordered his sons to listen to him and told them that a great treasure lay hidden in the land. He added that he was going to leave it to them. At that, the sons asked their father how they would find that. Then the old man told them that they had to dig the land for that.

Explanation:
The correct answer is that they must dig the land, because the old man clearly says the treasure lies hidden there and instructs them, “You must dig the land for it.” This tests reading comprehension: you infer the required action directly from the speaker’s words in the dialogue.

Question #160 (ID: 481591)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“What are you doing now, Rashed?” I said. “I am watching an interesting program on television.” “Aren’t you wasting your time?” “No, I don’t think so,” he said. “Remember, too much watching of TV makes people lazy.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
I asked Rashed what he was doing then. He replied that he was watching an interesting programme on television. I asked him again if he was not wasting his time. He replied in the negative and said that he did not think so. Then I advised him to remember that too much watching TV makes people lazy.

Explanation:
Explanation: In reported speech we normally shift tenses back, change pronouns and time words, and use appropriate reporting verbs. So “What are you doing now?” becomes He asked Rashed what he was doing then; “I am watching…” becomes He said (that) he was watching an interesting programme; “Aren’t you wasting your time?” becomes I asked if/whether he was wasting his time, and “No, I don’t think so” becomes He replied that he didn’t think so. Note: general truths (e.g., “makes people lazy”) are often backshifted to past (“made”) in reported speech, though they can stay in the present if still considered universally true.

Question #161 (ID: 481592)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“Dear friend, which book do you want?” “A Practical English Grammar’ of A. J. Thomson. I lost my copy yesterday,” said Oishe. “I can lend you. But return it in a week,” I said.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Addressing Oishe as dear friend, I asked her which book she wanted. She replied that she wanted A Practical English Grammar' of A.J. Thomson. She added that she had lost her copy the day before yesterday. Then I told her that I could lend her, and also told her to return it in a week.

Explanation:
Use "I can lend it to you" because "lend" normally takes a thing as a direct object; if you don’t name the thing you must say "it" (or include the object, e.g. "I can lend you my copy"). The book title should be marked (e.g. 'A Practical English Grammar') and the author is introduced with "by" rather than "of". In direct speech, when a sentence is followed by a reporting tag (like "said Oishe" or "I said"), replace the final full stop with a comma inside the closing quote: "I can lend it to you, but return it in a week," I said.

Question #162 (ID: 481593)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
“Why did you not go to school yesterday, Rimu?” asked the mother. “I was ill, mum.” “How are you today?” “Well,” answered the girl. “Don’t worry for me.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The mother asked/enquired of/demanded of Rimu why she (R) had not gone to school the previous day. Addressing the mother as mum Rimu replied that she (R) had been ill. The mother again asked/enquired of/demanded of the girl how she (R) was that day. The girl replied/answered that she (R) was well and also told/requested not to worry for her/forbade to worry for her.

Explanation:
Correct, because Rimu herself says she missed school yesterday due to illness: "I was ill." Her answer "Well" shows she is better today, and "Don't worry for me" is a reassurance to her mother, so the dialogue gives the past reason for absence and the present condition.

================================================================================
Question #163 (ID: 481594)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
The teacher said to the boy, “Do you know that honesty is the best policy?” The boy said, “Yes, sir, I think so.” “Then learn to be honest from your boyhood,” said the teacher. “Thank you, Sir,” said the boy. “May Allah grant you a long life,” said the teacher to boy.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The teacher asked the boy if he (b) thought that honesty is the best policy. The boy respectfully replied in the affirmative and said that he thought so. Then the teacher advised him (b) to be honest from his boyhood. The boy respectfully thanked him (t). The teacher prayed for the boy that Allah might grant him a long life.

Explanation:
Explanation: A yes/no question like "Do you know that honesty is the best policy?" is reported as "He asked the boy if/whether he knew that honesty was the best policy" because the question form changes to statement order and present tense shifts to past (is → was) under sequence of tenses. Likewise, "Yes, sir, I think so" becomes "the boy said/replied that he thought so" (think → thought); imperative/advice "Then learn to be honest from your boyhood" is reported as "the teacher advised him to learn to be honest from his boyhood"; "Thank you, Sir" becomes "the boy thanked him"; and the wish "May Allah grant you a long life" is reported as "the teacher prayed/wished that Allah might grant him a long life" (may → might).

(d) People like it most on a moonlit night. (চাঁদনী রাতে লোকেরা এটি সবচেয়ে বেশি পছন্দ করে।)

Finally, check that the combined parts produce a logical idea; if not, swap parts until you get six natural sentences.

Question #165 (ID: 481531)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make six sentences using the parts of sentences from each column of the table below:


[Image]


Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Matching:

(a) Tree plantation is very essential for balanced environment. (ভারসাম্যপূর্ণ পরিবেশের জন্য বৃক্ষরোপণ খুবই প্রয়োজনীয়।)

(b) Trees provide us with wood, fruits and flowers. (গাছ আমাদের খাদ্য, ফল ও ফুল সরবরাহ করে।)

(c) Deforestation is opposite to tree plantation. (বন উজাড় বৃক্ষরোপণের বিপরীত।)

(d) Afforestation is called the air purifier. (বনায়নকে বায়ু পরিশোধক বলে।)

(e) Cutting trees is dangerous for the environment. (গাছ কাটা পরিবেশের জন্য বিপজ্জনক।)

(f) It is the main cause of environmental pollution. (এটি পরিবেশ দূষণের প্রধান কারণ।)

Explanation:
প্রশ্নের সঠিক উত্তরগুলো সেই কারণে ঠিক যে প্রতিটি বাক্যবিষয়ের বাম কলামের অংশটি একটি সম্পূর্ণ বিষয়/বিবরণ এবং ডান কলামের অংশটি সেই বিষয়ের সঙ্গে মিল রেখে পূর্ণক্রিয়া বা পরিপূর্ণ অর্থ দেয় — ফলে মিলিয়ে একটি সম্পূর্ণ বাক্য তৈরি হয়। বাক্য গঠনের সময় কালের সঙ্গতিপূর্ণতা, বিষয়-ক্রিয়ার মিল (subject–verb agreement) এবং যৌক্তিক সংযোগ বজায় রাখলে বাক্যগুলো Grammatically ঠিক এবং অর্থপূর্ণ হয়। সুতরাং প্রতিটি বাম অংশকে উপযুক্ত ডান অংশের সঙ্গে যুক্ত করে যথাযথ শাব্দিক পরিবর্তন ও রুচিসম্পন্ন বিরামচিহ্ন দিয়ে ছয়টি ঠিকঠাক বাক্য পাওয়া যায়।

Question #166 (ID: 481530)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make six sentences using the parts of sentences from each column of the table below:


[Image]


Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Matching:

(a + v + iii) = Football is a popular game. (ফুটবল একটি জনপ্রিয় খেলা।)

(b + i + iv) = Previously it was mainly played by the male players. (পূর্বে এটি প্রধানত পুরুষ খেলোয়াড়দের দ্বারা খেলা হতো।)

(c + ii + i) = But nowadays it is played worldwide by the female players also. (কিন্তু বর্তমানে বিশ্বব্যাপী এটি নারী খেলোয়াড়দের দ্বারাও খেলা হয়।)

(d + iii + vi) = A few months ago our women's football team defeated the Nepalese team by 3-1 goals in the final match and became champion. (কয়েক মাস আগে আমাদের মহিলা ফুটবল দল 'ফাইনাল ম্যাচে নেপালী দলকে ৩-১ গোলে পরাজিত করে চ্যাম্পিয়ন হয়েছিল।)

(e + vi + ii) = They were not defeated in any match in SAFF Women's Championship-2022. (তারা SAFF Women's Chamoionship-২০২২-এ কোনো ম্যাচে পরাজিত হয়নি।)

(f + iv + v) = As soon as the champions touched down at the airport, thousands of excited fans cheered and waved the national flag to welcome them. (চ্যাম্পিয়নরা বিমানবন্দরে নেমে আসার সাথে সাথে হাজার হাজার উচ্ছ্বসিত ভক্ত উল্লাস করেছিলো এবং তাদেরকে স্বাগত জানাতে জাতীয় পতাকা দুলিয়েছিলো।)

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: প্রতিটি বাক্য তৈরি করতে টেবিলের প্রতিটি কলাম থেকে একটি অংশ বেছে নিয়ে তা মিলিয়ে একটি সম্পূর্ণ ভাব প্রকাশ করা হয়; সঠিক উত্তরগুলো তাই সঠিক কারণ এগুলোতে বিষয় (subject), ক্রিয়া (verb) ও বাকী অংশ মিলেমিশে সম্পূর্ণ এবং যুক্তিসঙ্গত ধারণা দেয়। বাক্য গঠন করার সময় বিষয় ও ক্রিয়ার একবচন/বহুবচন মিলিয়ে ক্রিয়ার রূপ ঠিক রাখুন, প্রয়োজনে সময় (tense) ও শব্দক্রম বদলান যাতে অর্থ পরিষ্কার থাকে।

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make six sentences using parts of sentences from each column of the table below:


[Image]


Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Matching:

(a) Punctuality is the habit of doing a thing in its exact time. (সময়ানুবর্তিতা হলো কোনো কাজ সঠিক সময়ে করার অভ্যাস।)

(b) It is a good habit. (এটি একটি ভালো অভ্যাস।)

(c) Nothing can be brought to a conclusion without punctuality. (সময়ানুবর্তিতা ব্যতীত কোনো কিছু সঠিকভাবে শেষ/ সম্পাদন করা যায় না।)

(d) In a wide sense, it denotes the process for proper utilization of time. (ব্যাপক অর্থে এটি সময়ের সঠিক ব্যবহারের জন্য প্রক্রিয়াটিকে নির্দেশ করে।)

(e) Maintaining punctuality is necessary for all human beings. (সময়ানুবর্তিতা বজায় রাখা সকল মানুষের জন্য প্রয়োজনীয়।)

(f) So, one should form the habit of being punctual from one's childhood. (তাই, শৈশব থেকেই প্রত্যেকেরই সময়নিষ্ঠ হওয়ার অভ্যাস গড়ে তোলা উচিত।)

Explanation:
সঠিক বাক্যগুলো সেই সব অংশের সংমিশ্রণ যেগুলো মিলিয়ে একটি পূর্ণাঙ্খল বাক্য তৈরি করে — অর্থাৎ প্রথম কলামের বিষয়/বিষয়বাচক অংশ এবং দ্বিতীয় কলামের ক্রিয়া/বিবরণ একটি স্বতন্ত্র ভাব প্রকাশ করতে হবে। বাক্য খুঁটিনাটি পরীক্ষা করে দেখুন: বিষয় ও ক্রিয়ার একবচন/বহুবচন ও কাল মিলছে কী না, শব্দগুলোর মধ্যে যৌক্তিক সংযোগ আছে কী না; পড়লে স্বাভাবিক অর্থ বের হলে সেটাই সঠিক মিল। প্রয়োগে প্রতিটি সম্ভাব্য জোড়া পড়ে অনুভব করুন — ভাষাগত সঙ্গতি ও স্পষ্ট অর্থ থাকলেই বাক্যটি গ্রহণযোগ্য।

Explanation:

Make six sentences using the parts of sentences from each column of the table below:


[Image]

(b) Newspaper is called the store house of knowledge. (সংবাদপত্রকে জ্ঞানের ভান্ডার বলা হয়।)

(c) It broadens our outlook and enriches our wisdom. (এটা আমাদের দৃষ্টিভঙ্গিকে প্রসারিত করে এবং আমাদের জ্ঞানকে সমৃদ্ধ করে।)

Explanation:

Question #170 (ID: 481465)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards: Mymensingh Board | Tags: Mymensingh Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Fill in the blanks with the words from the box. You may need to change the forms of some of the words:


[Image]


A student must have the habit of reading newspaper everyday. Mere (a)________ knowledge is not enough in this (b)__________ world. Newspapers help him (c)___________his general knowledge and make him aware of the (d)___________issues both inside and outside the country. A man who doesn't read (e)__________is like a frog in a narrow (f)___________ Being ignorant of the (g)____________ affairs, he (h)____________ take part in the talks and discussions in an enlightened society and feels like a fish out of (i)_____________By reading newspapers one can widen one's range of (j)_____________ in the field of science, history, geography, literature etc.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Gap filling with suitable words:

A student must have the habit of reading the newspaper every day. Mere (a) bookish knowledge is not enough in this (b) competitive world. Newspapers help him (c) enrich his general knowledge and make him aware of the (d) current issues both inside and outside the country. A man who doesn't read (e) newspapers is like a frog in a narrow (f) well. Being ignorant of the (g) burning affairs, he (h) cannot take part in the talks and discussions in an enlightened society and feels like a fish out of (i) water.

Ans. (a) bookish; (b) competitive; (c) enrich; (d) burning; (e) newspaper; (f) well; (g) current; (h) cannot; (i) water; (j) knowledge.

Explanation:
These words fit both meaning and grammar: 'bookish' contrasts with the practical demands of the 'modern' world; newspapers 'enrich' a student's general knowledge and make him aware of 'current' issues; the proverb needs 'newspapers' and 'well' (a frog in a narrow well), and being ignorant of 'national' affairs he 'cannot' take part in discussions and feels like a fish out of 'water'; finally 'knowledge' correctly completes the idea of widening one's range.

Question #171 (ID: 481466)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Modern civilization is the (a) — of science. Science has worked (b) — a magician in the world. We can’t do even a (c) — day without the help of science. Many quick means (d) — communication like telephone, telex, fax, telegram, satellite, etc. are (e) — greatest wonders of science. Nowadays, a message can be sent from one corner of the world to another in the twinkle of (f) — eye. Science has brought a revolutionary (g) — in all fields. In the field of medical science, (h) — has got eyes, lame has got legs, deaf has got hearing power. (i) — diseases which were incurable in the past are now easily (j) —.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
Explanation: 
(a) product — "product of science" is the usual collocation; (b) like — shows comparison "worked like a magician"; (c) single — "not even a single day" is the correct phrase; (d) of — "means of communication" is the fixed expression; (e) the — superlative needs the definite article "the greatest"; (f) an — the phrase is "twinkle of an eye"; (g) change — "revolutionary change" is the standard collocation; (h) the blind — "the blind" refers collectively to blind people; (i) many — "many diseases" fits; (j) cured — past participle meaning made healthy. These choices follow common collocations, article usage, and correct noun/verb/participle patterns.

Nowadays, a good number of farmers are getting benefits (a) — the organic cultivation of vegetables. Vermicompost, (b) — organic fertilizer made mainly (c) — cowdung and earthworm is used by the farmers. As the farmers did not use (d) — chemical fertilizer or pesticides on their vegetable beds, the (e) — cost has come down. It takes (f) — fifty thousand taka to prepare an acre of (g) — and the harvest starts within forty-five days (h) — planting. Due to good yield of the crop, some temporary warehouses have been made in (i) — area. So, proper (j) — of organic fertilizer can change the scenario of our agricultural sector.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:

Question #175 (ID: 481470)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Patriotism is an (a) — quality of human being. It creates in a man a feeling of love for his motherland. It is older than (b) —. The man who loves his own country, does his first and (c) — duties and works for the (d) — and (e) — of his country, is a patriot. Even the ancient tribes had a great love for the land where they were born and sacrificed their lives to (f) — it. If he does and (g) — his duties honestly and sincerely in his own fields, he can be a patriot. If he does not do so, he will be a (h) —. We must not have bitterness towards anyone. But (i) — patriotism is very bad. All should (j) — off it from their hearts.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা:

ক জন্মগত — দেশপ্রেম সাধারণত মানুষের মধ্যে স্বভাবতই থাকে, তাই এটি “জন্মগত” মানে প্রকৃত উপযুক্ত।  

খ ইতিহাস — প্রাচীন উপজাতিগুলোও জন্মভূমির প্রেম পেত, তাই দেশপ্রেম লেখচিত্র বা নথি হওয়ার আগেও অর্থাৎ ইতিহাসের চেয়েও পুরোনো।  

গ প্রধান — বাক্যটি “first and ___ duties” অর্থে, এখানে “প্রধান” বা “principal/foremost” দায়িত্ব বোঝায়।  

ঘ কল্যাণ — দেশপ্রেমিক দেশের উন্নতি ও জনকল্যাণে কাজ করে, তাই “কল্যাণ” সঙ্গত।  

ঙ সমৃদ্ধি — দেশের উন্নতি뿐 아니라 আর্থিক ও সামাজিক সমৃদ্ধির জন্যও কাজ করা patriotism-এর লক্ষণ, তাই “সমৃদ্ধি” মানায়।  

চ রক্ষা — প্রাচীনরা জন্মভূমিকে বাঁচাতে জীবন ত্যাগ করেছে, অর্থাৎ তারা সেটি “রক্ষা” করত।  

ছ পালন — নিজের ক্ষেত্রের কাজ নিষ্ঠার সাথে “পালন” করলে সে দেশপ্রেমিক বলা যায়; এখানে কাজ করা ও দায়িত্ব পালন বোঝানো হয়েছে।  

জ দেশদ্রোহী — যদি কেউ দায়িত্ব পালন না করে তাহলে সে দেশপ্রেমী হবে না; এমন নৈরাজ্যপূর্ণ অথবা দেশের প্রতি অবাধ্যতা হলে তাকে “দেশদ্রোহী” বলা যায়।  

ঝ সংকীর্ণ — সীমিত বা অন্যদের বিরোধী হওয়া জাতীয়তাবাদ খারাপ; তাই “সংকীর্ণ” দেশপ্রেম নিন্দনীয়।  

ঞ দূর করে ফেলতে — বাক্যটি কাউকে মনের ভেতর থেকে সেই নেতিবাচক মনোভাব “দূর করে ফেলতে” বলছে, অর্থাৎ তা ত্যাগ করতে হবে।

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Adopting unfair means in the examination is (a) — offence. It degrades (b) — standard of education. If the students of (c) — country do not acquire (d) — education, there will be no development for (e) — country. (f) — examinee should study seriously so that he can cut (g) — good figure in the examination. To acquire true education should be (h) — only aim in the lives of all students. (i) — educated man cannot support adopting (j) — unfair means in the  examination at all.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: শব্দের স্বর-ধ্বনি ও নির্দিষ্ট/অনিির্দিষ্টতা অনুযায়ী আর্টিকেল নির্বাচন করা হয় — (a) ও (i)-তে শব্দটি স্বরধ্বনিতে শুরু হওয়ায় "an" লাগে (an offence, an educated man)। (b), (e) ও (h)-এ বিশেষ বা পরিচিত বস্তু বোঝানো হয়েছে তাই "the" ব্যবহার করা হয় (the standard, the country, the only aim)। (c) ও (g)-এ অপরিচিত একক বস্তু বোঝাতে "a" লাগে (a country, a good figure), আর (f)-এ প্রতিটি পরীক্ষার্থী বোঝাতে "every" সঠিক। (j)-এ "unfair means" একটি সাধারণ বহুবচন/অপরিব্যক্ত ধারণা, তাই সাধারণত কোনো আর্টিকেল লাগে না।

Terrorism is a (a) — threat and major concern (b) — almost all the countries. Terrorists damage (c) — human lives and properties (d) — panic and terror. The cause of terrorism mainly (e) — to the deprivation of genuine rights and also greed and exploitation (f) — groups and nations. Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:

Question #178 (ID: 481473)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Once a farmer had a great desire (a) — land. One day (b) — to the landlord, he wanted some land (c) — he might live in comfort. The landlord was very wise. So, he told him to have as much land as he could cover by running (d) — sunset. The farmer became very pleased (e) — that. Next morning he started running as (f) —as he could to cover more area. He ran till evening and the sun was (g) — to set. He ran with his last strength but became very tired and fell (h) — dead. He was (i) — there. Then the wise man remarked a man needs just as much land as will be enough (j) — his grave.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
বিস্তারিত ব্যাখ্যা: এখানে প্রতিটি শূন্যে বাক্যের সম্পর্ক অনুযায়ী উপযুক্ত প্রস্তাববাচক বা ক্রিয়া বসে — উদাহরণ: "desire for" (এখানে [math]'for'[/math] কারণের জন্য), "he went" ([math]'went'[/math] ক্রিয়া নির্দেশে), "so that" ([math]'so\;that'[/math] উদ্দেশ্য প্রকাশে)। সময় ও মাত্রা বোঝাতে "before" ([math]'before\;sunset'[/math]), "as fast as" ([math]'as\;fast\;as'[/math]) ও "about" ([math]'about\;to\;set'[/math]) লাগে; অবস্থা প্রকাশে "at" ([math]'pleased\;at'[/math]), "down" ([math]'fell\;down\;dead'[/math]) এবং পরিণতিতে "buried" ও শেষে পুনরায় "for" ([math]'enough\;for\;his\;grave'[/math]) সঠিক। এই শব্দগুলোকে উপলব্ধি করলে প্রত্যেক শূন্যের মানে ও ব্যবহার পরিষ্কার হয়ে যায়।

Question #179 (ID: 481474)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Road accident is (a) — regular phenomenon in Bangladesh. Many people die (b) — road accidents every year. So, it is considered as a (c) —. Road accidents occur for (d) — reasons. Many factors are (e) —for road accidents. The most common cause is (f) — driving. Sometimes they drive night coach (g) — on the same day. The drivers do not check the engines (h) — before they start driving. The roads are two-lane roads (i) — any dividers. These are some of the (j) — reasons of road accidents in Bangladesh.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) use "a" because "regular phenomenon" is a singular count noun and needs an article; (c) and (j) use adjectives like "major"/"main" to show the seriousness.  
(b) "in" is the correct preposition with "die" and "road accidents"; (d) "various" or "many" fits because multiple causes exist; (e) "responsible" commonly collocates with "for" (f) "reckless" or "careless" describes the driving cause; (g) "as well" (or "also") shows they do both shifts on the same day; (h) "properly" is an adverb modifying "check"; (i) "without" expresses the absence of dividers.

Housing is one of the greatest (a) — in our country. Thousands of people in big (b) — like Dhaka and Chattogram (c) — in the footpaths. In rural (d) — there is also an acute (e) — of housing. The cost of construction is (f) — day by day. At present it is very (g) — for the (h) — people to (i) — the cost of construction. So, this problem (j) — to be solved soon.

Question #181 (ID: 481476)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Nowadays, the young farmers of our country are showing interest to (a) — foreign vegetables. They with their innovative power, have added new dimensions (b) — the country’s agricultural sector. Karim Ullah is such a (c) —. Five years ago, he started his farm with a (d) — and challenge. Now he owns a (e) — farm where he cultivates curry leaves, lemon grass, broccoli and other (f) — vegetables. The cultivation of foreign crops (g) — our country is very inspiring for both (h) — farmers and the customers as it brings diversity in our regular (i) — and nutrition. It is also possible to (j) — vegetables by ensuring quality production and packaging.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
ক "cultivating" নির্বাচন করা হয়েছে কারণ বাক্যে বিদেশি সবজি চাষ করার আগ্রহ বোঝাতে ক্রিয়ার প্রয়োজন এবং "interest in cultivating" হল সঠিক collocation।  
খ "to" সঠিক কারণ "add dimensions to" একটি স্থায়ী ইংরেজি প্রবাদবাক্য — কোনো কিছুকে অন্য কিছুর উপর প্রভাবিত বা সংযোজন হিসেবে বলা হয়।  
গ "young farmer" উপযুক্ত কারণ প্রসঙ্গে নতুন ও উদ্ভাবনী ফসল চাষকারী যুবককে নির্দেশ করা হচ্ছে।  
ঘ "dream" রাখা হয়েছে কারণ কোনো ব্যাক্তি সাধারণত একটি স্বপ্ন বা লক্ষ্য নিয়েই খামার শুরু করে; এখানে ধারণাগত অনুপ্রেরণা বোঝাতে এটি মানানসই।  
ঙ "commercial" ফার্ম মানে বাণিজ্যিকভাবে পরিচালিত খামার, যেটা বিদেশি উদ্ভিদগুলোর ব্যাপক চাষের বাস্তব প্রতিফলন।  
চ "exotic" ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে কারণ curry leaves, lemongrass, broccoli ইত্যাদি দেশের প্রচলিত সবজির থেকে ভিন্ন বা বিদেশি—অর্থাৎ "exotic" মানায়।  
ছ "in" প্রয়োজন কারণ এখানে বলা হচ্ছে বিদেশি ফসলের চাষ ঘটছে আমাদের দেশের মধ্যে: "cultivation of foreign crops in our country"।  
জ "local" সঙ্গত কারণ বাক্যে স্থানীয় কৃষকরা এবং গ্রাহকদের উভয়কেই অনুপ্রাণিত করে—সুতরাং "local farmers" মানানসই।  
ঝ "diet" নেওয়া হয়েছে কারণ এখানে নিয়মিত খাদ্যাভ্যাস ও পুষ্টি সম্পর্কে বলা হচ্ছে, তাই "diet" শব্দটি পুরোপুরি মেলে।  
ঞ "export" উপযুক্ত কারণ মানসম্মত উৎপাদন ও প্যাকেজিং নিশ্চিত করলে ওই সবজি বিদেশে বিক্রি করা যায়—অর্থাৎ রপ্তানি করা সম্ভব।

Question #182 (ID: 481477)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
A true friend is (a) — asset. He stands (b) — his friends in time (c) — danger. He is not (d) — greedy person. He (e) — wishes for the welfare of (f) — friend. But it is a matter of (g) — regret that a true friend is very (h) — today. A selfish man cannot be a (i) — friend. He always thinks of his (j) — interest.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
A true friend is an asset. He stands by his friend in time of the danger. Normally he is not a greedy person. He always wishes for the welfare of his friends. But it is a matter of fact that an ideal friend is very rare today.

Explanation:

In the above sentences, the correct use of articles is to be mentioned.
There are three articles used in English Grammar.
'A', 'an' and 'the' are the three articles.
They are used with the nouns to specify their definiteness in the sentences.
'The' is the definite article.
'A' and 'an' are the indefinite articles.
'A' is used with words beginning with a consonant sound.
'An' is used with words beginning with a vowel sound.

Explanation:
Answers: a valuable, b by, c of, d a, e always, f his, g great, h rare, i true, j own. 

Reason: these choices fit common English collocations and grammar—'valuable' describes an asset, we say 'stand by' and 'time of', articles/possessives ('a', 'his', 'own') complete the noun phrases, 'always' shows habitual action, and 'great regret' + 'rare' and 'true' contrast correctly with 'selfish'.

By doing all (i) — thing, a student can hope to make (j) — excellent result.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) in; (b) an; (c) hard; (d) beginning; (e) text; (f) without; (g) from; (h) of/over; (i) these; (j) an.

Explanation:

(b) an — Use [math]"an"[/math] before a word beginning with a vowel sound like "easy."

(f) without — "Memorize answers without understanding" needs [math]"without"[/math] to show absence of understanding.

(h) of — "A good command of English" uses [math]"of"[/math] to show the language possessed.  
(i) these — "All these things" refers to the actions just listed, so [math]"these"[/math] is correct.  
(j) an — Use [math]"an"[/math] before the vowel sound in "excellent" (an excellent result).

Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) said/known/thought/considered; (b) the; (c) deviates/detaches; (d) of/called; (e) loved/respected/honoured/believed/liked; (f) all/everybody/everyone/anyone/anybody; (g) none/nobody; (h) Even/The; (i) honest; (j) in.

Explanation:
The phrase "Honesty is said to be the best policy" uses the fixed passive "said to be" and the definite article "the"; "strays from the path of morality" uses the correct verb + preposition ("stray from") and the possessive "of"; "admired by many but hated by some" is a natural contrast, "Some enemies..." introduces that contrast again, "honest and truthful" are the correct adjectives, and "throughout our life" correctly expresses duration. These choices follow normal English collocations and grammar, so they clearly convey that honesty is recommended and should be maintained for life.

(a) tree; (b) When; (c) produce; (d) seeds; (e) vanilla; (f) added; (g) origin; (h) brought; (i) Later; (j) chocolate.

The correct words fit the meaning and grammar of the passage: (a) "tree" because cacao is a tree; (b) "When" introduces the time clause; (c) "bear" (produce) fits with "pods"; (d) "beans" are the seeds collected from pods; (e) "powdered" (modifies "milk") is a common form added; (f) "added" correctly describes putting ingredients with the seeds; (g) "history" suits the sentence about how chocolate came to be; (h) "brought" shows Columbus carried cacao beans to Spain; (i) "Later" indicates a subsequent time; and (j) "chocolate" is what was changed from liquid to solid.

Question #214 (ID: 481461)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Fill in the blanks with the words from the box. You may need to change the forms of some of the words:


[Image]


All we know that mobile phone is the most (a)________ invention of modern science. Now a days, it is very (b)_________for us. At (c)_________ it is very small and light. (d)_________ changes have been brought about in (e)__________ communication by mobile phone. The whole (f)________ has now become smaller and (g)___________ unbelievably in respect of communicating information. But it is (h)___________ to say that mobile phone has some (i)__________ too. Over all, it is a great (j)__________ for mankind.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Gap filling with suitable words:

(a) wonderful; (b) essential; (c) present; (d) Revolutionary; (e) social; (f) world; (g) closer; (h) needless; (i) demerits; (j) blessing.

Explanation:
Solution words: (a) valuable, (b) useful, (c) present, (d) great, (e) mass, (f) world, (g) closer, (h) true, (i) disadvantages, (j) blessing.

Explanation: Each chosen word fits common collocations and meaning—"most valuable" shows importance, "useful for us" describes purpose, and "At present" is the correct time phrase. "Great changes" and "mass communication" are standard phrases; "world" and "closer" describe how communication has shrunk distances. Finally "true to say" is an idiom, "disadvantages" is the opposite of advantages, and "blessing" summarizes the overall positive effect.

Question #216 (ID: 481460)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Fill in the blanks of the following text with the clues given in the box:


[Image]


Examination is the process of (a)________the academic knowledge of the (b)___________ So, it should be absolutely (c)_________The authority should conduct and (d)__________it in the best possible (e)__________Adopting unethical activities in the (f)_________ is a great offence. It (g)_________the standard of education. In (h)_________of the students' failure to (i)__________true education, the nation will (j)_________ greatly. So all students should make the best use of time in order to be truly educated.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Gap filling with suitable words:

(a) assessing; (b) learners; (c) fair; (d) supervise; (e) way; (f) examination; (g) degrades; (h) case; (i) acquire; (j) suffer.

Explanation:
Explanation: The passage talks about what an examination does and its consequences, so (a) "assess" or "test" fits because an exam measures academic knowledge, and (b) "students" (or "candidates") are the people being assessed. (c) "fair" or "impartial" is required for correctness, and the authority must (d) "administer" or "supervise" it in the best (e) "manner" or "way" — these words fit both grammar and meaning. Cheating "in the exam" (f) is an offence because it (g) "lowers" or "undermines" the standard of education, and (h) "in consequence of" students' failure to (i) "acquire" or "receive" true education, the nation will (j) "suffer" greatly — each choice matches the intended sense and sentence structure.

Question #217 (ID: 481458)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Fill in the blanks with the words from the box. You may need to change the forms of some of the words:


[Image]


The Padma multi-purpose bridge has opened a new (a)................. in the history of Bangladesh. This (b)................. project has been implemented (c)............... any foreign aid. The southern 21 districts were cut (d)................... from the mainland by the mighty Padma river. So; this vast area could not keep pace with the other parts(e)................. economic development. But, direct connection with the capital by this bridge is going to expand (f)................ and commerce. Besides, (g)............... is also going to speed up. All these are contributing a lot to our economic (h)................ and surely reduce the (i)................... of those regions. The construction of the bridge which was our long-cherished. (j)................. at last came true.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Gap filling with suitable words:

(a) era; (b) mega; (c) without; (d) off; (e) considering; (f) trade; (g) tourism; (h) growth; (i) poverty; (j) dream.

Explanation:
(a) "era", (b) "ambitious" and (c) "without" fit because "opened a new era" is a common collocation, the bridge is a large-scale (ambitious) project, and "implemented without any foreign aid" is grammatically correct.

(f) "trade" and (g) "communication" work since bridges "expand trade and commerce" and speed up communication/transport.  
(h) "growth", (i) "poverty" and (j) "dream" fit common collocations: "economic growth", "reduce the poverty" and "long‑cherished dream" which "came true."

(a) — there can be no denying the fact (b) — they too possess equal rights and duties (c) — men do. They have noble mission to fulfill as men. (d) — they get opportunity, their genius, powers (e) — capacities will bloom fully.

(c) — a man is educated in the true sense, he will be able to lead a life completely different from others. (d) — he can distinguish between right and wrong. (e) — education is very important.

Options:


Correct Answer:

(a) Undoubtedly/In fact; (b) But; (c) If/When; (d) Besides/Therefore; (e) So/Thus.

Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board

Question:
A healthy man can do any work (a) —- he can eat any food he likes. (b) —-, he can enjoy life in every way. (c) —- an unhealthy man is unhappy, for he cannot eat and do what he likes. (d) —- he lives and dies poor. He may have intelligence, merit, learning and power, but he cannot put them to the use and reap their benefits. (e) —- health is the source of all happiness in life.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) In addition/Besides/And; (b) Moreover/Besides/So; (c) On the other hand/But/On the contrary; (d) As a result/Consequently/Thus; (e) That is why/Therefore/In fact/Above all/Actually/So.

Explanation:
Correct answers: (a) "and", (b) "besides", (c) "but", (d) "and", (e) "therefore". These fit because "and"/"besides" add positive points about a healthy man, "but" introduces the contrast with an unhealthy man, the second "and" continues the negative consequence, and "therefore" gives the concluding result.

Question #221 (ID: 481429)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
It is known to all that gold is a valuable metal. (a) —-, there are many metals cheaper than gold though they like it. (b) —- they glitter for sometimes, they fade away in the long run. In our society there are also many people (c) —- are outwardly very gentle and polished. Later on their real identity is revealed (d) —- they do not exercise moral values. That’s why, people say, “ All (e) —- glitters is not gold.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) But/However/Besides; (b) As/Though; (c) who; (d) as/because/If; (e) that.

Explanation:
Explanation: a "However" fits because it contrasts the next idea with the previous statement. b "Although" introduces a concession (they may glitter but still fade). c "who" is the correct relative pronoun for people, and d "that" introduces the reported fact about their morals. e "that" is needed in the fixed proverb "All that glitters is not gold."

Question #222 (ID: 481430)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Summer noon is very painful and disgusting. (a)----- the sun shines hotly over head, life becomes miserable. The sufferings of the people know no bounds (b)------ the electricity goes off. (c) ----- the people use hand fans to fan themselves. Children can neither sleep (d)----- read. They feel out of sorts. (e)----- the poor suffer most. They work outside in the burning sun.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) When/While/Since/As; (b) when; (c) Then; (d) nor; (e) But/Mainly/Specially/Above all.

Explanation:
(a) "When" — it introduces the time/condition (when the sun shines hotly) that makes life miserable.  
(b) "when" — it again shows the time/condition causing greater suffering (when the electricity goes off).  
(c) "then" — it expresses the result/consequence of the power cut (people then use hand fans).  
(d) "nor" — it pairs with "neither" to show two things children cannot do (neither sleep nor read).  
(e) "especially" — it emphasizes that the poor are affected most because they work outside in the heat.

Question #223 (ID: 481431)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
The rapid growth of population must be controlled. (a)----- all sorts of attempts to solve food problem will fail. (b)----- we have to increase our food production very rapidly. We may mostly; solve our food problem by changing our traditional food habit. (c) ------, we can take potato instead of rice. (d)------ it is high time we changed our eating habit. (e)------ food can help to solve our food problem to a great extent.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Otherwise; (b) At the same time/Moreover/Besides: (c) For example/For instance; (d) So; (e) Last of all/Because/Moreover.

Explanation:
(a) Otherwise — নির্দেশ করে যে জনগণ নিয়ন্ত্রণ করা না হলে ফলাফল হিসেবে খাদ্য সমস্যার সব চেষ্টাই ব্যর্থ হবে।  
(b) Therefore — পূর্বের অবস্থার ফলে যে সিদ্ধান্ত আসে তা বোঝায়: খাদ্য উৎপাদন দ্রুত বাড়াতে হবে।  
(c) For example — উদাহরণ হিসেবে নতুন খাবার নেওয়ার কথা বলার জন্য ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে (যেমন আলু বদলে চাল)।  
(d) Indeed — বক্তব্যটির তাত্ক্ষণিকতা ও জোরদার করার জন্য উপযুক্ত সংযোগকারী।  
(e) Such food — পূর্বে উল্লিখিত বিকল্প খাবারগুলো নির্দেশ করে; এই ধরনের খাবার খাদ্য সমস্যার সমাধানে অনেক সহায়তা করতে পারে।

Once upon a time there lived a fox (a)----- was very clever. He lived in a jungle in a very hot country (b)----- Bangladesh. One day, (c) ----- Mr. Fox was walking through the jungle, he fell into a trap. After trying very hard he could get out of the trap (d) ----- lost his tail. Without his tail Mr. Fox looked very strange (e)----- he felt very sad and ashamed.

(a) which/that; (b) like; (c) while; (d) but; (e) as well as/and/and so/for which.

Question:
Summer noon is very painful and disgusting. (a) — the sun shines hotly over head, life becomes miserable. The sufferings of the people know no bounds (b) — the electricity goes off. (c) — the people use hand-fans to fan themselves. Children can neither sleep (d) — read. They feel out of sorts. (e) — the poor suffer most. They work outside in the burning sun.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
a "when" fits because it introduces the time clause showing when life becomes miserable. b "especially when" emphasizes that suffering gets worse at the time the electricity fails. c "so" shows the result—people use hand-fans because of the heat and power cut. d "nor" is needed to complete the pair "neither...nor" (Children can neither sleep nor read). e "Moreover" (or "Besides") adds an additional point stressing that the poor suffer most.

Question #231 (ID: 481439)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Truthfulness is the greatest of all virtues. (a) — we do not cultivate the habit of speaking the truth, we cannot command the confidence of others. A lie never lies hidden. (b) —, it will come out today or tomorrow. (c) —, all despise him without considering his social status. The habit of speaking the truth, (d) —, must be formed from the very childhood. We should know (e) — speaking the truth is the most rewarding thing in life.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) "If" introduces the conditional cause—without cultivating truthfulness we cannot win others’ confidence.  
(b) "So" and (c) "then" show natural consequences: a lie will be exposed, and then people despise the liar.  
(d) "Therefore" is a parenthetical result linking the preceding points to the necessity of forming the habit early, and (e) "that" correctly introduces the noun clause "that speaking the truth..."

Question:
A school magazine is a magazine (a) — is published by the school authority annually. It contains poems, articles, essays and jokes. The publication of it is not an easy task (b) — it needs time, energy and money. (c) — a magazine committee is formed from the teachers and the students. The editor (d) — is selected or elected by the committee members, invites writings. (e) — good writings are selected for printing.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
Explanation:
a Use "that"/"which" because a relative pronoun is needed to introduce the defining clause "is published by the school authority". 
b Use "because" since it gives the reason why publication is not an easy task. 
c Use "so"/"therefore" to show the result (a committee is formed). 
d Use "who" because it refers to a person (the editor) in a relative clause. 
e Use "then" to indicate sequence (after inviting writings, good ones are selected).

Global warming is increasing day by day (a) — deforestation. We cut down trees (b) — never think of planting more trees. (c) — human and other living beings are in the threat of extinction. Time is coming (d) — there will be no tree left for us. (e) — we have to face bitter consequence of deforestation.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
Use "due to" in (a) because it shows the cause; "and" in (b) to join the two actions; "consequently" or "as a result" in (c) to show the effect; "when" in (d) to introduce the time clause; and "then" in (e) to indicate the consequent result.

Question #234 (ID: 481442)

Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board

Question:
The whole world has turned into a global village (a) — the improvement of information technology. Now we can know (b) — is happening on the other corner of the world sitting at home. One culture is coming in touch with another. The poor culture is receiving quickly the elements (c) — are available in rich culture. (d) — technology transforms culture and develops it. (e) — we have to prevent the infiltration of bad culture of another society to our own culture.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
Explanation: For (a) a causal phrase like "due to" / "because of" / "owing to" is required to show the reason (improvement of IT). For (b) an indirect question needs "what" — "what is happening." For (c) a relative pronoun with plural agreement is needed, so "that are" or "which are" (because "elements" is plural). Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board

Climate change means the changes in climate. (a) — climate on earth is constantly changing. (b) — climate change, the weather pattern in any specific region on earth prevails (c) — across the whole earth is changing. Human activities are greatly responsible for it. We are cutting down trees for habitation and agricultural purpose. (d) — use of chemicals in industries causes serious harm to the ozone layer. (e) — there is a rapid increase in temperature causing greenhouse effect the ozone layer a purpose.

ঙ ফলত গ্রিনহাউস গ্যাস বাড়ে এবং তাপমাত্রা দ্রুত বাড়ার মাধ্যমে গ্লোবাল ওয়ার্মিং সৃষ্টি হয়, যা মূল বষয়টির সারমর্ম তুলে ধরে।

People usually want to have their own way. They want to think and act (a) — they like. (b) — one cannot have one’s own way all the time. (d) — these decisions ought not to be unjust (e) — harmful to others.

Question:
(a) — taking food, we should bear in mind (b) — we do not eat just to satisfy hunger or to fill the belly. We eat (c) — we can preserve our health. Some people living in the midst of plenty, do not eat the food they need for good health (d) — they have no knowledge of the science of health and nutrition. (e) — they suffer from various diseases.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) While/At the time of; (b) that; (c) so that/in order that; (d) because/as/since; (e) As a result/ Consequently/So/Therefore.

Explanation:
Explanation: The best words are (a) "Before" because it indicates the time prior to taking food; (b) "that" because it introduces the clause explaining what we should bear in mind; (c) "so that" (or "in order that") because it expresses purpose—why we eat; (d) "because" since it gives the reason they do not eat properly; (e) "therefore" (or "consequently") because it shows the result—that they suffer various diseases.

Question #241 (ID: 481449)

Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board

Question:
Ripa is a student of class ten. (a) — she is meritorious, she never takes pride in her merit. She is helpful to all. (b) — any weak student comes to her with any problem, she tries to help him. She is respectful of the senior (c) — affectionate to the junior. She is simple in behaviour (d) — strict in principle. (e) — everyone loves her.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Though/Although; (b) If/When; (c) and; (d) but; (e) So/Therefore/Thus/Hence.

Explanation:
Explanation: (a) "Although" is correct because it shows contrast between being meritorious and not taking pride. (b) "When" or "if" fits because it introduces a condition/time — whenever a weak student comes, she helps. (c) "And" links two similar positive traits, (d) "but" shows contrast between simple behaviour and strict principles, and (e) "so" (or "therefore") shows the result that everyone loves her.

Question #242 (ID: 481450)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
We know that trees are essential for all kinds of creatures. They give us not only food (a) — oxygen. They protect us from natural calamities. (b) — , they are called the saviour of our environment. (c) — many people are not aware of this. They cut down trees randomly. (d) —, forest lands are shrinking. (e) — people go on cutting down trees, one day there well be no trees left for us.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) but also; (b) That's why/For this reason; (c) But; (d) So; (e) If.

Explanation:
Explanation:
(a) "but also" is correct because it completes the correlative pair "not only ... but also" to add another important item.  
(b) "therefore" fits because it shows a logical result — since trees protect us, they are called saviours.  
(c) "however" is appropriate to show contrast between what is true about trees and the fact that many people are unaware.  
(d) "consequently" (or "as a result") is right because it links the action (cutting trees) to its outcome (shrinking forest lands).  
(e) "if" is correct since the sentence expresses a conditional situation: continuing the action will lead to no trees left.

Globalization is a term (a) — is commonly used by man. (b) — it is a process of expanding trade and commerce all over the world creating a borderless market. (c) — global development we have conquered the time (d) — distance. (e) —, we can learn that is happening in the farthest corner of the world.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:

Explanation:
(a) "which" is correct because it introduces a non-restrictive relative clause describing "term"; (b) "as" correctly links the reason/explanation ("as it is a process..."); (c) "With" shows accompaniment ("With global development..."); (d) "and" joins the two items "time" and "distance"; (e) "thus" (or "therefore") correctly signals the result ("thus we can learn what is happening...").

None can deny the importance of tree plantation (a) — our lives on earth directly or indirectly depend on it. (b) — it is a matter of sorrow that we are cutting down trees indiscriminately. Question:
Gold is a bright precious metal. There are many metals cheaper (a) — gold but look like it. They glitter well (b) — fade in course of time. Actually there are many people in our society (c) — are outwardly gentle and nice. But (d) — a period of time, their real identity is revealed. (e) —, all that glitters is not gold.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) than; (b) but; (c) who; (d) after; (e) So/Actually/In fact/Therefore.

Explanation:
Correct fill-ins are: (a) "than", (b) "but", (c) "who", (d) "after", (e) "Hence". "Than" is needed for comparison ("cheaper than gold"), "but" shows contrast, "who" introduces the relative clause describing people, "after" indicates a lapse of time, and "Hence" signals the concluding inference.

Question #250 (ID: 481418)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Honesty is a divine virtue. The man (a) — possesses this quality is the happiest person in the world. To be honest, man should have trustworthiness (b) — nobody trusts a liar. (c) — Allah helps the honest people. (d) — children should be taught honesty from the very beginning of life. (e) — they should be taught discipline.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) who; (b) because/since/as; (c) In fact/Moreover/Besides; (d) So; (e) Therefore/In fine/ finally.

Explanation:
Use "who" for (a) because it introduces a relative clause describing "man" ("The man who possesses…"). Use "because" for (b) since it gives the reason; use "Indeed" for (c) to affirm the statement; use "Therefore" for (d) to show the conclusion drawn from the previous points; and use "Also" (or "Besides") for (e) to add another related point.

An idle man does not do his work in right time. He puts off work of today for tomorrow. A student (a) — neglects his daily lessons is sure to fail. A young man who idles away his time becomes a burden to the family (b) — the society. His brain becomes the workshop of Devils. It is said (c) — the Devil tempts the busy man (d) — the idle man tempts the Devil. (e) — everyone should make the best use of time.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) who; (b) as well as/and; (c) that; (d) whereas/and/but/while/on the other hand/on the contrary; (e) So/For this reason.

Explanation:
Explanation: 
(a) "who" is the correct relative pronoun for a person and introduces the clause "who neglects his daily lessons." (b) "and to" links two prepositional phrases—"to the family" and "to the society." (c) "that" introduces reported speech, (d) "but" shows the contrast between the two ideas, and (e) "Therefore" gives the logical conclusion that everyone should make the best use of time.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:

Explanation:

(c) — it has become a great concern to all. (d) — solving this problem some necessary steps should be taken. In this regard general people should help the government. (e) — the population growth is controlled, people will lead a happy life.

Options:


Correct Answer:

সঠিক ক্রম: ক → খ → গ → ঘ → ঙ। প্রথমে সাধারণ বক্তব্য দেয়া হয়েছে (ক), এরপর সেটি ব্যাখ্যা ও বিশদ করা হয়েছে (খ), তারপর সমস্যার গুরুত্ব বলা হয়েছে (গ)। পরবর্তীতে সমাধানের পদক্ষেপ ও মানুষের সহযোগিতা বলা হয়েছে (ঘ) এবং শেষে সমস্যার নিয়ন্ত্রণের ফলে কি ফল পাওয়া যাবে তা উল্লেখ করা হয়েছে (ঙ)—এটাই লজিক্যাল ও ধারাবাহিক সাজানো।

Question #256 (ID: 481424)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
A hare is a very speedy animal. (a)----- a tortoise moves very slowly. (b)------, it has a heavy shell on its back. (c)----- its legs are short. (d) -----, it cannot move as fast as other animals. One morning a hare laughed at a tortoise for its slow motion. The hare asked the tortoise to run a race. (e)----- the tortoise felt hurt, it agreed to the proposal of the hare.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) On the contrary/But; (b) Firstly: (c) Secondly; (d) So/As a result; (e) Though/Although.

Explanation:
The correct connectors are: (a) "Whereas" to show contrast with the hare; (b) "Besides" and (c) "Moreover" to add additional reasons for the tortoise's slowness; (d) "Therefore" to express the result that it cannot move as fast; and (e) "Although" to show concession (it felt hurt but still agreed). These choices fit the logical relations in the passage: contrast, addition, result, and concession.
