Question #301 (ID: 481358)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2022 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) The government has almost completed the construction of the Padma Bridge. (Passive)

(b) This is the largest bridge of Bangladesh. (Comparative degree)

(c) The countrymen will be very happy when it will be opened for use. (Exclamatory)

(d) It is a mega project. (Negative)

(e) We should go to visit it. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) The construction of the Padma Bridge has been almost completed by the government.

(b) This is larger than any other bridge of Bangladesh.

(c) How happy the countrymen will be when it will be opened for use!

(d) It's not a small project.

(e) Let us go to visit it.

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা:

ক The construction of the Padma Bridge has almost been completed by the government. Passive করতে কৃতকারক (the government) কে "by" নিয়ে বাক্যের শেষে রাখা হয় এবং মূল বাক্যের অবজেক্ট (the construction) কে সাবজেক্ট করা হয়; টেন্স অর্থাৎ present perfect রাখতে "has been completed" ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে এবং "almost" যথাযথভাবে "been"–এর আগে রাখা হয়েছে। 

খ This bridge is larger than any other bridge in Bangladesh. Comparative degree এ তুলনা দেখাতে "larger than" ব্যবহৃত হয়—superlative "largest" বদলে comparative দিয়ে দুটি বা ততোধিক বস্তুর মধ্যে তুলনা করা হয়। 

গ How happy the countrymen will be when it is opened for use! Exclamatory sentence তৈরিতে "How + adjective + subject + verb" প্যাটার্ন ব্যবহার করা হয়; পাশাপাশি "when it is opened"—এখানে ভবিষ্যৎকলের জন্য "will" পুনরাবৃত্তি দরকার নেই। 

ঘ It is not a mega project. Negative বানাতে "is" এর পরে "not" যোগ করা হয়ে বাক্যকে নেগেটিভ করা হয়। 

ঙ Let's visit it. Imperative বা আদেশ/পরামর্শ জানাতে প্রথমপদে "Let's" (let us) ব্যবহার করলে "আমরা যাই"—ধরনের অনুরোধ/আদেশ প্রকাশ পায়; সংক্ষিপ্ত করে "Let's visit it." বলা যায়۔

Question #302 (ID: 481359)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2022 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) The freedom fighters are considered to be the real heroes of our country. (Active)

(b) Their contribution will never be forgotten. (Affirmative)

(c) Their sacrifice is greater than any other thing. (Positive)

(d) By taking proper steps, we can improve their condition. (Negative)

(e) We must show proper respect to them. (Passive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) We consider the freedom fighters to be the real heroes of our country.

(b) Their contribution will always be remembered.

(c) No other thing/ Nothing is as great as their sacrifice.

(d) Without taking proper steps, we cannot improve their condition.

(e) Proper respect must be showed to them.

Explanation:
Explanation:
(a) Active: Change the passive verb phrase "are considered to be" into an active clause with an agent: "People consider the freedom fighters the real heroes of our country." The subject of the passive becomes the object and a doer (people) is added.

(b) Affirmative: Replace the negative idea "will never be forgotten" with an affirmative equivalent: "People will always remember their contribution." "Never forgotten" ↔ "always remembered" changes negation to affirmation.

(c) Positive: Turn the comparative "is greater than any other thing" into the positive degree: "Their sacrifice is great." This removes the comparative structure and uses the base adjective.

(d) Negative: Introduce negation using an auxiliary or a clause like "unless": "Unless proper steps are taken, we cannot improve their condition." The negative is formed by "cannot" (or by adding "not") and/or by using "unless."

(e) Passive: Make the object the subject and keep the modal verb "must": "They must be shown proper respect." The original object ("them") becomes the subject of the passive and "must" remains with the past participle.

Question #303 (ID: 481360)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2022 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Computer is one of the greatest inventions of modern science. (Positive)

(b) Computer is a blessing on earth. (Negative)

(c) We must learn how to use computer. (Imperative)

(d) Computer helps us a lot. (Passive)

(e) Because of its usefulness, it has become very popular. (Exclamatory)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Very few inventions of modern science are so/as great as computer.

(b) Computer is not a curse on earth.

(c) Let us learn how to use computer.

(d) We are helped a lot by computer.

(e) How popular it has become because of its usefulness!

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা:
ক বাক্যটি কোনো নেতিবাচকতা ছাড়া একটি সাধারণ ঘোষণা/ধনাত্মক বাক্য, তাই "Positive" সঠিক।  
খ বাক্যটিও ধনাত্মক; এতে নেগেটিভ কোনো উপাদান নেই, তাই "Negative" ভুল — সঠিক হলো ধনাত্মক/ঘোষণামূলক।  
গ "We must learn..." একটি বাধ্যতামূলক/দাবি বোঝানো বাক্য (modal/obligation), এটি সরাসরি আদেশ-ধর্মী নির্ম্দেশ নয়, তাই "Imperative" সঠিক নয়।  
ঘ "Computer helps us a lot." এ বাক্যে বিষয় (computer) কাজটি করছে, তাই এটি সক্রিয় কণ্ঠ (active voice); "Passive" ভুল।  
ঙ বাক্যটি কেবল কারণে বোঝাচ্ছে এবং সাধারণ ঘোষণামূলক; আগ্রহ বা বিস্ময়ের চিহ্ন নেই, তাই "Exclamatory" ভুল।

Question #304 (ID: 481361)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2022 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Honesty is the best way of leading life. (Positive)

(b) This noble virtue is always appreciated. (Active)

(c) Honesty can open a door of peace before a person. (Negative)

(d) Honesty is a very important virtue. (Exclamatory)

(e) So, we should never be dishonest. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) No other way of leading life is so/as good as honesty.

(b) People always appreciate this noble virtue

(c) Honesty cannot close a door of peace before a Person.

Or, Can't honesty open a door of peace before a person?

Or, Dishonesty can't open a door of peace before a person?

Or, It is not that honesty can't open a door of peace before a person.

(d) What an important virtue honesty is!

(e) So, let us not ever be dishonest.

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা:

ক ধনাত্মক (affirmative) বাক্য হলো নেগেটিভ কনট্রাকশন ছাড়া সরাসরি কোনো কথা বলার বাক্য; "Honesty is the best way of leading life." কোনো না নেই, তাই এটি ধনাত্মক বাক্য।  

খ সক্রিয় (active) বাচ্য হলে বিষয়টি কাজ করে; passive "is appreciated" কে active করে বানালে হবে "People always appreciate this noble virtue." — এখানে subject (people) কাজটি করছে, তাই active।  

গ নেতিবাচক (negative) বাক্যে না/কেনই বা বিরোধী অংশ থাকে; "Honesty can open..." এর নেতিবাচক হবে "Honesty cannot open a door of peace before a person." — এখানে "cannot" যোগ হওয়ায় বাক্যটি নেগেটিভ হয়ে গেছে।  

ঘ উত্সাহসূচক (exclamatory) বাক্য অনুভূতি প্রকাশ করে এবং বিস্ময়চিহ্ন (!) দিয়ে শেষ হয়; উদাহরণ: "What a very important virtue honesty is!" — এর ভাষা শক্তভাবে অনুভূতি প্রকাশ করছে, তাই exclamatory।  

ঙ অনুদের (imperative) বাক্য আদেশ বা নির্দেশ দেয় এবং সাধারণত ক্রিয়াপদ দিয়ে শুরু হয়; "Never be dishonest." এভাবে সরাসরি নির্দেশ থাকার কারণে এটি imperative।

Question #305 (ID: 481362)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2022 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Flower cultivation is very profitable now. (Exclamatory)

(b) Many people cultivate flowers for earning money. (Passive)

(c) At present, there is a great demand of flowers. (Interrogative)

(d) Everybody becomes glad to get flowers. (Negative)

(e) In some cases, flowers are more welcoming than any other gift. (Positive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) How profitable now flower cultivation is!

(b) Flowers are cultivated by many people for earning money.

(c) Isn't there a great demand of flower at present?

(d) There is nobody but becomes glad to get flowers.

Or, Nobody becomes sad to get flowers.

(e) In some cases, no other gift is as welcoming as flowers.

Explanation:
(a) This sentence shows strong feeling, so use an exclamatory form: "How profitable flower cultivation is now!"  

(b) In the passive the object "flowers" becomes the subject and the verb changes to passive: "Flowers are cultivated by many people to earn money."  

(c) To make it interrogative invert "there is" to "Is there" and place the time phrase appropriately: "Is there a great demand for flowers at present?"  

(d) To make it negative use a negative auxiliary: "Not everybody becomes glad to get flowers."  

(e) To put the comparative into the positive degree use the "No other ... as ... as" structure: "In some cases, no other gift is as welcoming as flowers."

Question #306 (ID: 481363)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Tarin. (Compound)

(b) Though she was a nice little girl, she was not an ordinary child. (Simple)

(c) She passed her time in reading and writing. (Interrogative)

(d) Her parents liked her very much. (Negative)

(e) Everyone praised her. (Passive)

(f) She was very attentive to her study. (Exclamatory)

(g) She also helped her mother in her free time. (Complex)

(h) She never told a lie. (Interrogative)

(i) She was one of the most intelligent girls in the school. (Positive)

(j) She worked hard to shine in life. (Complex)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Once upon a time there was a little girl and her name was Tarin.

(b) In spite of being a nice little girl, she was not an ordinary child.

(c) Didn't she pass her time in reading and writing?

d) Her parents did not dislike her at all.

e) She was praised by everyone.

f) How attentive she was to her study!

g) She also helped her mother when she was free.

h) Did she ever told a lie?

(i) Very few girls in the school were as intelligent as she.

j) She worked hard so that she could shine in life.

Explanation:
Explanation:
a This is a simple (declarative) sentence because it contains one independent clause; "Once upon a time" is just an introductory phrase, not a second clause.  
b This is a complex sentence because it has a subordinate clause introduced by "Though" ("Though she was a nice little girl") plus a main clause ("she was not an ordinary child"). The subordinate clause depends on the main clause, so the sentence is complex.  
c This is a simple declarative sentence with one independent clause stating an action; it is not a question.  
d This is an affirmative (positive) sentence because it states something directly without negation; the subject "Her parents" performs the action "liked."  
e This is active voice, not passive, because the subject "Everyone" performs the action "praised" rather than receiving it.  
f This is a simple declarative sentence (not exclamatory); it states a fact about her attentiveness in a neutral tone.  
g This is a simple sentence with a single independent clause ("She also helped her mother in her free time"), so it is not complex.  
h This is a negative declarative sentence because the adverb "never" negates the verb "told"; it is not an interrogative (no question form).  
i This expresses a superlative idea ("one of the most intelligent"), so it is not the positive degree; "most" shows a highest degree of comparison.  
j This is a simple sentence: one main clause ("She worked hard") with an infinitive phrase ("to shine in life") as purpose, but no additional clause, so it is not complex.

Question #307 (ID: 481364)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Mymensingh Board | Tags: Mymensingh Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Cricket is a very exciting game. (Exclamatory sentence)

(b) People of all ages enjoy this game. (Passive voice)

(c) It is played all over the world. (Active voice)

(d) At present, it is the most popular game in our country. (Comparative Degree)

(e) Though cricket is a costly game, people of all classes enjoy playing it. (Simple sentence)

(f)The game is played between two teams each consisting of eleven players. (Complex sentence)

(g) There are two umpires who conduct the game. (Simple sentence)

(h) It is full of thrill and excitement for the spectators. (Interrogative sentence)

(i) Bangladesh is a test-playing country developing its standard day by day. (Compound sentence)

(j) We must try our best to improve its present position. (Negative sentence without changing meaning)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
a To make it exclamatory we express strong feeling by using an exclamation or exclamatory structure, e.g. “What an exciting game cricket is!” or “Cricket is a very exciting game!” with an exclamation mark.

b In passive voice the object becomes the subject and we add “by …”, so “People of all ages enjoy this game” becomes “This game is enjoyed by people of all ages,” which shows the action received by the subject.

c Active voice names the doer as the subject; the active form is “People play it all over the world,” where “people” perform the action on “it.”

d Comparative degree uses “more … than” instead of “most,” so say “At present, it is more popular than other games in our country,” which directly compares two or more items.

e A simple sentence contains a single independent clause; combining the ideas without a subordinating conjunction gives a simple form like “Cricket is a costly game enjoyed by people of all classes,” using a participial phrase to keep it one clause.

f A complex sentence has a main clause plus a subordinate clause; for example, “The game is played between two teams, each of which consists of eleven players” has the main idea and a relative clause giving extra information.

g A simple declarative form removes the relative clause: “Two umpires conduct the game.” This is one independent clause stating a single fact.

h An interrogative sentence inverts the auxiliary and subject: “Is it full of thrill and excitement for the spectators?” uses subject–auxiliary inversion and a question mark to ask about the state.

i A compound sentence joins two independent clauses with a coordinating conjunction: “Bangladesh is a test-playing country, and it is developing its standard day by day,” which links two equal ideas.

j To make it negative without changing the meaning use a phrase that denies failure, e.g. “We must not fail to try our best to improve its present position,” which keeps the original obligation but in negative form.

Question #308 (ID: 481365)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Terrorism is a devastating phenomenon of the modern world. (Exclamatory)

(b) At present, it is called a challenge to fight against it. (Active)

(c) Who is not now in the threat of violence? (Assertive)

(d) Terrorism is more disastrous than anything. (Positive)

(e) It is one of the most corrosive problems of the modern world. (Comparative)

(f) Nobody wants his children to be terrorist in future. (Interrogative)

(g) Though there is law to punish the terrorists, it is not properly applied. (Simple)

(h) By applying the law properly, we can get rid of it. (Complex)

(i) We have to create social awareness to fight against corruption. (Compound)

(j) We all should avoid the killers of mankind. (Negative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
ক The sentence is a simple declarative (assertive) statement giving information and ends with a full stop, so it is not exclamatory; an exclamatory sentence would show strong emotion and use an exclamation form. 

খ This is passive voice: the verb phrase "is called" shows the subject receives the action; an active form would be "People call it a challenge." 

গ It is an interrogative sentence because it begins with the question word "Who" and asks a question, so it cannot be classified as assertive. 

ঘ The adjective "more disastrous" expresses comparison, so the sentence is comparative in degree, not positive. 

ঙ The phrase "one of the most corrosive" uses the superlative "most," so this is a superlative-degree expression, not merely comparative. 

চ This is an assertive (declarative) negative idea—"Nobody wants…" states a fact and ends with a period, so it is not interrogative. 

ছ The sentence contains a subordinate clause introduced by "Though…" plus a main clause, so it is a complex sentence rather than a simple one. 

জ Although it begins with a participial phrase ("By applying the law properly"), the structure has only one independent clause ("we can get rid of it"), so grammatically it is a simple sentence. 

ঝ This line expresses a single idea with one independent clause ("We have to create…"), so it is a simple sentence, not a compound sentence. 

ঞ The sentence gives a positive/affirmative instruction ("should avoid"), so it is not negative; a negative sentence would include words like "not" or "never."

Question #309 (ID: 481366)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Health is wealth. (Make complex sentence)

(b) A healthy poor man is happier than a sick moneyed man. (Use positive degree)

(c) Though a healthy man is an asset to his family, an unhealthy man is a liability. (Make compound sentence)

(d) He can succeed in life. (Make interrogative sentence)

(e) So, everybody cannot but be conscious of his health. (Make affirmative sentence)

(f) Everybody must take care of his health all the time. (Make negative sentence)

(g) Health can be improved by regular physical exercise and a balanced diet. (Use active voice)

(h) People who are poor cannot afford to take a balanced diet. (Make simple sentences)

(i) They are very concerned with the quantity of food. (Make exclamatory)

(j) Everybody should know it that malnutrition causes weakness. (Use passive voices)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) Because health is wealth, one should take care of it.
Explanation: This is a complex sentence because it has a subordinate clause ("Because health is wealth") that gives a reason and a main clause ("one should take care of it").

(b) A healthy poor man is not less happy than a sick moneyed man.
Explanation: The positive degree uses the base adjective "happy"; adding "not less" expresses the same comparison without using the comparative form "happier."

(c) A healthy man is an asset to his family, but an unhealthy man is a liability.
Explanation: This is a compound sentence formed by joining two independent clauses with the coordinating conjunction "but."

(d) Can he succeed in life?
Explanation: Forming an interrogative here requires inverting the auxiliary "can" and the subject "he."

(e) So, everybody must be conscious of his health.
Explanation: "Cannot but be conscious" means "must be conscious," so removing the negation yields the affirmative form.

(f) Everybody must not neglect his health at any time.
Explanation: A negative construction that preserves the original meaning uses "must not neglect" to show prohibition/avoidance.

(g) Regular physical exercise and a balanced diet can improve health.
Explanation: Changing to active voice makes the agents ("regular physical exercise and a balanced diet") the subject that performs the action on "health."

(h) People are poor. They cannot afford to take a balanced diet.
Explanation: The relative clause ("who are poor") is split into a simple sentence about people’s condition and a separate simple sentence stating they cannot afford a balanced diet.

(i) How concerned they are about the quantity of food!
Explanation: An exclamatory sentence uses "How" + adjective to express strong feeling about their concern.

(j) It should be known by everybody that weakness is caused by malnutrition.
Explanation: The main clause is put into passive voice ("It should be known by everybody") and the fact is expressed passively ("weakness is caused by malnutrition").

Question #310 (ID: 481367)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Wherever we may cast our eyes, we notice the achievement of science. (Make it simple)

(b) The electricity lights both the streets and the houses. (Make it negative)

(c) The radio broadcasts news, songs and lectures. (Make it passive)

(d) There is cinema to delight in the evening. (Make it complex)

(e) Computer is one of the most important inventions of modern science. (Make it positive)

(f) Who can go without it? (Make it assertive)

(g) Internet is as important as computer. (Make it comparative)

(h) It helps us to know about the world. (Make it compound)

(i) It is greater than all other inventions of modern science. (Make it superlative)

(j) The invention of computer is a great miraculous event. (Make it exclamatory)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
a We see the achievements of science everywhere.
Explanation: The complex phrase "Wherever we may cast our eyes" is simplified to the clear subject–verb–adverbial order "We see ... everywhere," keeping the original meaning but using a simple sentence.

b The electricity lights neither the streets nor the houses.
Explanation: To make the sentence negative for both items we use the correlative negative "neither ... nor," which negates lighting of both streets and houses.

c News, songs and lectures are broadcast by the radio.
Explanation: In passive voice the objects ("news, songs and lectures") become the subject, the verb becomes "are broadcast," and the original subject ("the radio") follows with "by."

d There is cinema in the evening that people can enjoy.
Explanation: This makes the sentence complex by adding a subordinate relative clause "that people can enjoy," which gives additional information about the evening cinema.

e The computer is an important invention of modern science.
Explanation: Changing "one of the most important" to "an important" converts the sentence from a superlative/ordinal idea to the positive degree, stating importance simply.

f No one can go without it.
Explanation: An assertive sentence states a fact; replacing the question with the declarative "No one can..." asserts the intended meaning directly.

g The internet is more important than the computer.
Explanation: To make a comparative, use "more ... than" to compare the two items, replacing the equal comparison "as ... as."

h It helps us, and it informs us about the world.
Explanation: A compound sentence joins two independent clauses ("It helps us" and "it informs us about the world") with the coordinating conjunction "and."

i It is the greatest of all the inventions of modern science.
Explanation: To form the superlative, use "the greatest" plus "of all" to show it ranks above every other invention.

j What a great and miraculous event the invention of the computer is!
Explanation: An exclamatory sentence begins with "What" + adjective(s) + noun and then the subject and verb, expressing strong feeling about the event.

Question #311 (ID: 481368)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Haji Mohammad Mohsin was more gracious than any other man in this subcontinent. (Positive)

(b) He was born in Hoogli. (Complex)

(c) He inherited a vast property from his father and sister. (Interrogative without changing meaning)

(d) He did not misuse this wealth. (Passive)

(e) He is called a friend of humanity. (Active)

(f)He did not marry. (Affirmative)

(g) During his lifetime, he spent money lavishly to help the poor. (Compound)

(h) He was very kind to the poor: (Negative without changing meaning)

(i)One day when a thief entered his room, he caught him. (Simple)

(j)He caught the thief but did not punish him. (Complex)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) The original uses a comparative ("more ... than any other") which is equivalent to a superlative; to make the positive degree we use the base adjective with an intensifier (e.g. "very gracious"). This keeps the meaning but removes the comparative form.

(b) A complex sentence has a main clause plus a subordinate clause; add a relative or adverbial clause for extra information (e.g. "He was born in Hoogli, which is in Bengal") to make it complex.

(c) Past simple questions use the auxiliary "did" plus the base verb, so the interrogative form is "Did he inherit a vast property from his father and sister?" The main verb becomes the base form "inherit" and "did" marks the past.

(d) Passive of a past simple negative uses "was not" + past participle: "This wealth was not misused by him." The object becomes the subject and the agent is optional with "by."

(e) To change passive to active make the agent the subject: "People call him a friend of humanity." The verb changes accordingly and the object becomes the direct object.

(f) To express the same idea affirmatively without "not," use an adjective: "He remained unmarried." This affirmative form conveys the same meaning as "He did not marry."

(g) A compound sentence joins two independent clauses with a coordinating conjunction; e.g. "He spent money lavishly to help the poor, and people benefited greatly from his generosity." This preserves the original idea while adding a second independent clause.

(h) Use the negative of an antonym to keep the meaning: "He was not unkind to the poor." Saying "not unkind" expresses the same positive idea without the original phrasing.

(i) A simple sentence has one subject and one predicate; combine the actions around a single subject: "One day a thief entered his room and was caught." Here "a thief" is the single subject with a compound predicate, making the sentence simple.

(j) Use a subordinating conjunction to form a complex sentence showing contrast: "Although he caught the thief, he did not punish him." The subordinate clause ("Although he caught the thief") plus the main clause make it complex.

Question #312 (ID: 481369)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2020 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Man is the maker of his own fortune. (Interrogative)

(b) If he makes a proper use of his time, he is sure to prosper in life. (Simple)

(c) The person doing otherwise is sure to repent later. (Complex)

(d) The lazy suffer miserably in the long run. (Exclamatory)

(e)To kill time is to commit suicide. (Interrogative)

(f) Our life is nothing but a sum total of hours, days and years. (Assertive)

(g)Youth is the most valuable season of life. (Positive)

(h) In youth mind is soft and it can be shaped easily. (Simple)

(i) Unless you use the morning hours of life, you have to pay a heavy price afterwards. (Compound)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) This is an assertive (declarative) simple sentence because it states a fact with a single subject–predicate structure and ends with a full stop.

(b) This is a complex sentence: the subordinate conditional clause "If he makes a proper use of his time" depends on the main clause "he is sure to prosper in life," so there are two clauses with a dependent–independent relationship.

(c) This is a simple (assertive) sentence; "doing otherwise" is a participial phrase modifying "person," but the sentence contains only one main clause that makes a statement.

(d) This is an assertive simple sentence because it states a fact about a group in one independent clause; an exclamatory sentence would show strong emotion or use an exclamation mark.

(e) This is an assertive (declarative) sentence: an infinitive phrase serves as subject and predicate ("To kill time" = "to commit suicide"), so it makes a statement, not a question.

(f) This is an assertive (declarative) simple sentence because it gives a single factual statement about life in one main clause.

(g) This is an assertive sentence that uses the superlative degree ("most valuable"); it declares a fact and contains a superlative adjective, so it is not merely the positive degree.

(h) This is a compound sentence: it joins two independent clauses ("mind is soft" and "it can be shaped easily") with the coordinating conjunction "and."

(i) This is a complex sentence because the subordinate concessive/conditional clause "Unless you use the morning hours of life" depends on the main clause "you have to pay a heavy price afterwards," so one clause is dependent on the other.

Question #313 (ID: 481370)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Man is the best creation of God. (Comparative)

(b) Isn’t it our responsibility to do good deeds? (Assertive)

(c) Our life is not measured by months or years. (Active)

(d) Honest people lead a happy life. (Complex)

(e) It matters little if a man lives many years or not. (Interrogative)

(f) Nobody is absolutely happy on earth. (Affirmative)

(g)So, we should not waste time in vain. (Passive)

(h) If we use time properly, we can be benefited. (Simple)

(i) All men must die. (Negative)

(j) Though we take utmost care, we cannot avoid death. (Compound)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) "Man is the best creation of God." → Comparative: change the superlative "best" to the comparative "better" and add a comparison, e.g. "Man is better than other creations of God." This is because comparative degree (better) compares two or more items and uses "than" to show the comparison.

(b) "Isn’t it our responsibility to do good deeds?" → Assertive: make it a statement: "It is our responsibility to do good deeds." Turn the question into a declarative sentence by removing inversion and the negative auxiliary ("Isn't") and using the affirmative verb form.

(c) "Our life is not measured by months or years." → Active: make the agent the subject, e.g. "Nobody measures our life by months or years." Passive "is measured" becomes active "measures" and you supply a subject (nobody/people) while keeping the negation.

(d) "Honest people lead a happy life." → Complex: add a subordinate clause to show reason or condition, e.g. "Honest people lead a happy life because they have peace of mind." A complex sentence has one independent clause plus a dependent (subordinate) clause like "because…" to show cause or condition.

(e) "It matters little if a man lives many years or not." → Interrogative: form a question: "Does it matter if a man lives many years or not?" Turn the statement into a question by inserting the auxiliary "does" and inverting the subject and auxiliary.

(f) "Nobody is absolutely happy on earth." → Affirmative: express the same idea without a negative word, e.g. "Everyone has some unhappiness on earth." To convert a negative sentence to an affirmative equivalent, replace the negative subject ("nobody") with a positive subject ("everyone") and rephrase the predicate to keep the original meaning.

(g) "So, we should not waste time in vain." → Passive: make "time" the subject, e.g. "So, time should not be wasted in vain (by us)." In passive voice the object of the active sentence becomes the subject, and the verb becomes a form of "be" + past participle; the agent ("by us") is optional.

(h) "If we use time properly, we can be benefited." → Simple: convert to a single independent clause, e.g. "We can benefit by using time properly." A simple sentence has one independent clause, so combine the idea into one clause (using a gerund or rephrasing) and use active verb "benefit."

(i) "All men must die." → Negative: put the statement in negative form, e.g. "All men do not live forever." This negates the predicate ("do not live forever") while preserving the original sense that mortality is inevitable.

(j) "Though we take utmost care, we cannot avoid death." → Compound: join two independent clauses with a coordinating conjunction, e.g. "We take utmost care, yet we cannot avoid death." A compound sentence links two independent clauses of equal rank using conjunctions like "and," "but," or "yet."

Question #314 (ID: 481371)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Corruption is one of the worst evils. (Positive)

(b)A corrupt man can do anything against morality. (Complex)

(c) People hate a corrupt man. (Passive)

(d) Nobody respects him. (Interrogative)

(e) The man who takes bribe, is next to devil. (Simple)

(f) Though we have strict law, we are still affected by this evil. (Compound)

(g) No other person is as hated as a corrupt man. (Superlative)

(h) We hope that Bangladesh will be free from this evil. (Simple)

(i) Everybody avoids a corrupt man. (Negative)

(j) A corrupt man leads a very unhappy life. (Exclamatory)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা:

ক সঠিক: এটি একটি ইতিবাচক (affirmative) বাক্য কারণ বাক্যে নেগেশন নেই এবং একটি সরাসরি বক্তব্য করা হয়েছে।  

খ ভুল: বাক্যে কোনো উপনিবেশ (dependent clause) নেই, কেবল একটি প্রধান ক্রিয়া-বাক্য (modal + object) এবং একটি prepositional phrase রয়েছে; তাই এটি জটিল (complex) নয়, এটি সরল/simple বাক্য।  

গ ভুল: বাক্যটি active voice — subject "People" কাজটি করছে; passive হলে হবে "A corrupt man is hated by people." তাই এটি passive নয়।  

ঘ ভুল: "Nobody respects him." একটি ঘোষণামূলক (declarative) বাক্য, প্রশ্নবোধক হলে হবে "Does nobody respect him?" তাই এটি interrogative নয়।  

ঙ ভুল: বাক্যে "who takes bribe" নামধারা (relative clause) আছে, তাই এটি কেবল সরল বাক্য নয়; একটি উপবাক্যসহ হওয়ায় এটি complex sentence হিসেবে গণ্য হবে।  

চ ভুল: "Though we have strict law" একটি অসম্পূর্ণ (subordinate) concessive clause, এবং মূল বাক্য আছে — এটি compound নয়; এটি একটি complex বাক্য (subordinate + main clause)।  

ছ সঠিক: "No other person is as hated as a corrupt man." বাক্যটি তুলনামূলকভাবে সর্বোচ্চ ঘৃণার বিষয়টি প্রকাশ করে এবং অর্থটিতে superlative অর্থ আছে, তাই এটি superlative ধারণ করে।  

জ ভুল: বাক্যে প্রধান ধারা "We hope" এবং একটি that‑clause আছে ("that Bangladesh will be free…"), তাই এটি সরল নয়; এটি complex sentence (main + subordinate)।  

ট ভুল: "Everybody avoids a corrupt man." হল ইতিবাচক/affirmative বাক্য; নেতিবাচক (negative) হলে হবে "Nobody avoids…" বা "Everybody does not avoid…" তাই এটি negative নয়।  

ঠ ভুল: "A corrupt man leads a very unhappy life." একটি সাধারণ ঘোষণামূলক বাক্য;	exclamatory হলে বিশেষভাবে বিস্ময় বা শক্তি দেখাতে চিহ্ন ('How unhappy his life is!') ব্যবহার করা হয়, তাই এটি exclamatory নয়।

Question #315 (ID: 481372)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Patriotism is a noble virtue. (Interrogative)

(b) It is the greatest of all virtues in a man’s life. (Comparative)

(c) It persuades a man to do everything just. (Negative)

(d) This quality highly motivates á man so that he can sacrifice his life for the country. (Simple)

(e) What an outstanding quality it is! (Assertive)

(f) A man having patriotic zeal is called a patriot. (Complex)

(g) A patriot fears none but the Creator. (Affirmative)

(h) By paying taxes he obeys the law. (Compound)

(i) He is respected by all. (Active)

(j) So we should be patriots. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) The sentence is a declarative (assertive) simple sentence because it states a fact: subject + verb + complement, with no question or command.  
(b) This is a superlative (not comparative) declarative sentence because the word "greatest" shows the highest degree among all.  
(c) The sentence is affirmative (positive) and declarative because it affirms an action; there is no negation word like "not" or "never."  
(d) This is a complex sentence: the main clause ("This quality highly motivates a man") is followed by a subordinate purpose clause ("so that he can sacrifice his life for the country").  
(e) It is exclamatory because it expresses strong feeling using "What ...!" rather than making a plain statement.  
(f) Grammatically this is a simple sentence with a participial phrase ("having patriotic zeal") modifying "a man"; it does not contain a separate clause, so it is not complex.  
(g) The sentence is negative in meaning because "none" (no one) negates the verb—so it expresses negation rather than being purely affirmative.  
(h) This is a simple sentence: a single independent clause with an introductory adverbial phrase ("By paying taxes"); it is not two independent clauses joined, so it is not compound.  
(i) The sentence is passive voice because the subject ("He") receives the action ("is respected") rather than doing it; the active form would be "All respect him."  
(j) This is a declarative suggestion (modal statement) using "should," not an imperative command; an imperative would be "Be patriots."

Question #316 (ID: 481315)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Internet is a computer-based networking system. (Interrogative) (b) It is a speedy transmitting system of information. (Complex) (c) Its functions are smooth and rapid. (Negative) (d) A man has an Internet connection and gets a link soon according to his expectation. (Simple) (e) Many educational institutions are greatly benefited through the use of Internet. (Complex) (f) A student can visit all the renowned libraries of the world without going there. (Passive) (g) It plays an effective role in the field of trade and commerce. (Exclamatory) (h) E-commerce has become one of the most popular topics to the customers. (Positive) (i) It helps the customers to buy or choose anything without going to market. (Compound) (j) What an amazing milestone it is in the modern world of communication! (Assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Internet is a computer-based networking system. (Interrogative)

➡️ Isn’t the Internet a computer-based networking system?

(Or: Is the Internet not a computer-based networking system?)

(b) It is a speedy transmitting system of information. (Complex)

➡️ It is a system which transmits information speedily.

(c) Its functions are smooth and rapid. (Negative)

➡️ Its functions are not rough and slow.

(Alternative: There is no function of it that is not smooth and rapid.)

(d) A man has an Internet connection and gets a link soon according to his expectation. (Simple)

➡️ Having an Internet connection, a man gets a link soon according to his expectation.

(e) Many educational institutions are greatly benefited through the use of Internet. (Complex)

➡️ Many educational institutions are greatly benefited because they use the Internet.

(f) A student can visit all the renowned libraries of the world without going there. (Passive)

➡️ All the renowned libraries of the world can be visited by a student without going there.

(g) It plays an effective role in the field of trade and commerce. (Exclamatory)

➡️ What an effective role it plays in the field of trade and commerce!

(h) E-commerce has become one of the most popular topics to the customers. (Positive)

➡️ Very few topics are as popular to the customers as e-commerce.

(i) It helps the customers to buy or choose anything without going to market. (Compound)

➡️ It helps the customers to buy or choose anything, and they do not need to go to the market.

(j) What an amazing milestone it is in the modern world of communication! (Assertive)

➡️ It is a very amazing milestone in the modern world of communication.

Explanation:
ক এই বাক্যটি একটি বিবৃতি, প্রশ্ন করে না এবং প্রশ্নচিহ্ন নেই; তাই এটি প্রশ্নবাচক (interrogative) নয়।  
খ বাক্যটি একক স্বাধীন ক্লজ; কোনো উপবাক্য নেই, তাই এটা জটিল (complex) নয়—এটি সরল বিবৃতি।  
গ এখানে নেগেশন নেই; “smooth and rapid” ইতিবাচক বর্ণনা, তাই এটি ঋণাত্মক (negative) বাক্য নয়।  
ঘ ঠিক আছে — একটি বিষয় (A man) ও তার উপর ক্রিয়াসমূহ (has, gets) একই স্বাধীন ক্লজে আছে, ফলে এটি সরল বাক্য।  
ঙ বাক্যটিতে কেবল একটি স্বাধীন ক্লজ আছে এবং কোনো উপবাক্য নেই, তাই এটি জটিল (complex) বাক্য নয়।  
চ এখানে "A student" বিষয় হিসেবে কাজ করে এবং নিজেই ক্রিয়া করে (can visit), তাই এটি সক্রিয় (active) কণ্ঠে; passive হলে হবে যেমন: "All the renowned libraries can be visited by a student."  
ছ এটি সাধারণ বিবৃতি যা পিরিয়াডে শেষ হওয়া উচিত; বিস্ময়বোধ জাগানোর জন্যে exclamatory বাক্যে বিশেষ রূপ বা উদ্ঘাটক চিহ্ন (উদাহরণ: What an…) থাকে, তাই এটি exclamatory নয়।  
জ বাক্যটি ইতিবাচক/affirmative কারণ এতে কোনো negation নেই; “one of the most popular” থাকা সত্ত্বেও বাক্যটি নেগেটিভ নয়।  
ঝ এখানে একমাত্র স্বাধীন ক্লজ আছে; “buy or choose” কেবল যৌগিক ক্রিয়া/বস্তুর অংশ — compound sentence হলে দুটি স্বাধীন ক্লজ থাকা প্রয়োজন।  
ঞ "What an amazing milestone…!" হলো বিস্ময়বোধপূর্ণ উচ্চারণ এবং বিস্ময়বাচক চিহ্ন আছে, তাই এটি exclamatory; assertive (সাধারণ বিবৃতি) নয়।

Question #317 (ID: 481316)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Corruption is one of the worst evils. (Positive) (b) A corrupt man can do anything against morality. (Complex) (c) People hate a corrupt man. (Passive) (d) Nobody respects him. (Interrogative) (e) The man who takes bribe, is next to devil. (Simple) (f) Though we have strict law, we are still affected by this evil. (Compound) (g) No other person is as hated as a corrupt man. (Superlative) (h) We hope that Bangladesh will be free from this evil. (Simple) (i) Everybody avoids a corrupt man. (Negative) (j) A corrupt man leads a very unhappy life. (Exclamatory)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) This sentence uses "worst," the superlative form of the adjective "bad," so it expresses the highest degree and is a superlative sentence.  
(b) It is a simple sentence because it has a single independent clause (one subject and one predicate) and no subordinate clauses.  
(c) This is active voice: the subject "People" performs the action "hate"; the passive would be "A corrupt man is hated by people."  
(d) "Nobody respects him" is a negative declarative sentence because "nobody" negates the verb; an interrogative would ask, e.g. "Does anybody respect him?"  
(e) It is a complex sentence because the relative clause "who takes bribe" is a subordinate clause modifying "the man," attached to a main clause.  
(f) This is complex: "Though we have strict law" is a subordinate concessive clause and "we are still affected…" is the main clause, so they form a complex sentence (not a compound).  
(g) The phrase "No other person is as hated as a corrupt man" conveys that he is the most hated, i.e., it expresses a superlative comparison in meaning.  
(h) This is a complex sentence: the main clause "We hope" takes a subordinate noun clause "that Bangladesh will be free…" as its object, so it is not simple.  
(i) "Everybody avoids a corrupt man" is an affirmative simple sentence (one independent clause), so it is not negative.  
(j) This is a declarative/simple sentence stating a fact; an exclamatory version would use an exclamation form (e.g., "What an unhappy life a corrupt man leads!").

Question #318 (ID: 481317)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2019 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Facebook is a common social network. (Make it a negative sentence)

(b) Now, it is being used all over the world. (Make it an active voice)

(c) Everybody uses it. (Make it an interrogative sentence)

(d) There is no student without a smart phone. (Make it an affirmative sentence)

(e) Who does not like social network? (Make it an assertive sentence)

(f) Facebook is the best of all social networks. (Make it a positive degree)

(g) It gives pleasure but we cannot get freedom to use it. (Make it a simple sentence)

(h) Use it or you cannot keep pace with the modern world. (make it complex sentence)

(i) We can get many new pieces of information by using it. (Make it a compound sentence)

(j) Would that I could open a Facebook account. (Make it an assertive sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) Facebook is not a common social network.
Explanation: Form a negative by placing "not" after the verb "is" to negate the statement.

(b) Now, people are using it all over the world.
Explanation: Change passive to active by supplying a doer ("people") and using the active verb form ("are using").

(c) Does everybody use it?
Explanation: Make a present-simple question by adding the auxiliary "does" before the subject and using the base verb "use."

(d) Every student has a smart phone.
Explanation: Convert the negative expression "no student without" into an affirmative universal statement using "every" and "has."

(e) Nobody dislikes social networks.
Explanation: Change the interrogative "Who does not..." into a declarative by stating the negative in a simple affirmative clause ("Nobody dislikes...").

(f) Facebook is good.
Explanation: Replace the superlative "the best" with the positive (base) adjective "good" to express the positive degree.

(g) It gives pleasure and restricts our freedom to use it.
Explanation: Make a simple sentence by keeping one subject ("It") and giving it a compound predicate ("gives... and restricts..."), so only one independent clause remains.

(h) If you do not use it, you cannot keep pace with the modern world.
Explanation: Form a complex sentence by introducing a dependent conditional clause ("If you do not use it") and linking it to the main clause.

(i) We can get many new pieces of information by using it, and we can share them with others.
Explanation: Create a compound sentence by joining two independent clauses with "and," each clause able to stand alone.

(j) I wish I could open a Facebook account.
Explanation: Turn the optative/exclamatory "Would that I could..." into an assertive declarative by using "I wish..." to state the same desire.

Question #319 (ID: 481318)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2018 | Boards:  | Tags: All Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Very few conquerors of the world were so great as Taimur. (Superlative)

(b) The province of a powerful prince was once attacked by young Taimur. (Active)

(c) Entering the kingdom of the prince, he captured a large village. (Compound)

(d) The army killed Taimur’s all soldiers. (Passive)

(e) He disguised himself as a poor traveler to survive. (Complex)

(f) He came to a house and asked for something to eat. (Simple)

(g) There lived an old woman in the house. (Complex)

(h) The woman became sympathetic to see Taimur. (Interrogative)

(i) The food was very hot. (Exclamatory)

(j) Taimur was too hungry to wait. (Negative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Taimur was one of the greatest conquerors of the world.

(b) Once young Taimur attacked the province of a powerful prince.

(c) He entered the kingdom of the prince and captured a large village.

(d) Taimur's all soldiers were killed by the army.

(e) He disguised himself as a poor traveller so that he could/might survive.

(f) Coming to a house, he asked for something to eat.

(g) There lived in the house a woman who was old.

(h) In the house, there lived a woman who was old.

(h) Didn't the woman become sympathetic to see Taimur?

(i) How hot the food was!

(j) Taimur was so hungry that he could not wait.

Explanation:
a This expresses a superlative idea because it compares Taimur with almost all other conquerors ("very few ... so great as"), showing he stands at the highest degree of greatness.

b Incorrect — the sentence is passive: the subject ("The province") receives the action and the agent appears after "by" ("by young Taimur"); the active form is "Young Taimur once attacked the province of a powerful prince."

c Incorrect — this is complex, not compound: it has a main clause ("he captured a large village") and a dependent participial clause ("Entering the kingdom of the prince") that modifies it, so one independent plus one subordinate element.

d Incorrect — the sentence is active because "The army" is the doer performing the action "killed"; the passive version would be "All Taimur’s soldiers were killed by the army."

e Correct — it is complex: there is a main clause ("He disguised himself as a poor traveler") and a subordinate infinitive of purpose ("to survive"), so one independent clause plus a dependent purpose phrase.

f Correct — it's a simple sentence with one subject ("He") and a compound predicate ("came ... and asked"), so a single independent clause describing two actions by the same subject.

g Incorrect — this is simple, not complex: "There lived an old woman in the house" is a single independent clause (existential construction) with no subordinate clause.

h Incorrect — the sentence is declarative, not interrogative: it states a fact ("The woman became sympathetic...") and does not ask a question; an interrogative would use question word/order or a question mark.

i Incorrect — as written it is a declarative statement describing the food; an exclamatory sentence would show strong feeling or use exclamatory form (e.g., "How hot the food was!").

j Incorrect — the sentence uses the "too ... to ..." degree construction (affirmative) to show excess, not negation; a negative sentence would include "not" or another negative word.

Question #320 (ID: 481319)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) My friend invited me to pay a visit to Cox’s Bazar. (Make complex sentence)

(b) I was very glad. (Make negative sentence)

(c) I accepted the invitation. (Use passive voice)

(d) When I reached there, my friend received me cordially. (Make simple sentence)

(e) I was very excited to see the sea beach. (Make exclamatory sentence)

(f) It is the largest sea beach in the world. (Use positive degree)

(g) It is one of the most beautiful sea beaches in the world. (Use comparative degree)

(h) It is called the pleasure seekers’ paradise. (Use active voice)

(i) Every year a lot of people come to visit it. (Make compound sentence)

(j) If I could visit the sea beach! (Make assertive sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) My friend invited me that/ in order that/ so that I could/might pay a visit to Cox's Bazar.

Or. It is my friend who invited me to pay a visit to Cox's Bazar.

(b) I was not displeased/unhappy/sad at all.

(c) The invitation was accepted by me.

(d) My friend received me cordially at the time of my reaching there.

Or. Reaching there, my friend received me cordially.

(e) How excited I was to see the sea-beach!

(f) No other sea-beach in the world is so/as large as it.

(g) It is more beautiful than most other sea-beaches in the world.

(h) We/People call it the pleasure seekers' paradise.

(i) Every year a lot of people come here and (they) visit it.

(j) I wish I could visit the sea-beach.

Explanation:
(a) My friend invited me to pay a visit to Cox’s Bazar, which I gladly accepted.
Explanation: This is a complex sentence because it joins a main clause with a relative clause "which I gladly accepted," adding extra information about the invitation.

(b) I was not very glad.
Explanation: Adding "not" makes the sentence negative while keeping the same tense and subject.

(c) The invitation was accepted by me.
Explanation: Passive voice is formed by making the object ("the invitation") the subject and using the auxiliary "was" + past participle "accepted."

(d) My friend received me cordially.
Explanation: This is a simple sentence with one independent clause expressing a single complete idea.

(e) How excited I was to see the sea beach!
Explanation: An exclamatory sentence uses "How" + adjective to express strong feeling or surprise.

(f) It is a very large sea beach.
Explanation: The positive degree uses the base adjective "large" (here strengthened by "very") instead of the superlative "largest."

(g) It is more beautiful than many other sea beaches in the world.
Explanation: The comparative degree is formed with "more" + adjective and "than" to compare it with other beaches.

(h) People call it the pleasure seekers’ paradise.
Explanation: Active voice uses a clear subject ("People") performing the action ("call") on the object ("it").

(i) Every year a lot of people come to visit it, and they enjoy the beach.
Explanation: A compound sentence joins two independent clauses ("a lot of people come..." and "they enjoy...") with the coordinating conjunction "and."

(j) I wish I could visit the sea beach.
Explanation: This assertive (declarative) sentence states the speaker’s wish directly instead of the exclamatory form.

Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Mother Teresa is an icon to many people. (Make it interrogative sentence)

(b) She is respected by everybody. (Make it active)

(c) She is one of the greatest persons of the world. (Make it positive)

(d) She was very kind to the needy and the ill-fated. (Make it negative)

(e) She believes that charity is a great virtue. (Make it compound sentence)

(f) Actually Mother Teresa was a noble hearted person. (Make it complex sentence)

(g) Mother Teresa was a very passionate woman. (Make it an exclamatory sentence)

(h) She helped those who were helpless. (Make it a simple sentence)

(i) She set up “Nirmal Hridoy” in Kolkata. (Make it a compound sentence)

(j) Who does not know about the charity of Mother Teresa? (Make it assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Isn't Mother Teresa an icon to many people?

(b) Everybody respects her.

(c) Very few persons of the world are so great as she.

(d) She was not unkind at all to the needy and the ill-fated.

Or. She was never unkind to the needy and the ill-fated.

(e) Charity is a great virtue and she believes it.

(f) Actually Mother Teresa was a person who was noble-hearted.

Or, Actually it was Mother Teresa who was a noble-hearted.

(g) What a passionate woman Mother Teresa was!

(h) She helped the helpless/helpless people.

(i) She set up 'Nirmal Hridoy' and it was at Kolkata.

(j) Everybody knows about the charity of Mother Teresa.

Explanation:
(a) Is Mother Teresa an icon to many people?
Explanation: The sentence is made interrogative by inverting the auxiliary verb "is" and the subject "Mother Teresa".

(b) Everybody respects her.
Explanation: Converted the passive "is respected by everybody" into active voice by making "everybody" the subject and "respects" the verb.

(c) She is a great person.
Explanation: Changed from the superlative phrase "one of the greatest" to the positive degree "great", which is the required positive form of the adjective.

(d) She was not unkind to the needy and the ill-fated.
Explanation: Made the sentence negative by adding "not" and using the opposite "unkind" (litotes) to preserve the original meaning.

(e) She believes that charity is a great virtue, and others agree with her.
Explanation: Formed a compound sentence by joining two independent clauses with the coordinating conjunction "and".

(f) Mother Teresa was a noble-hearted person because she helped the poor.
Explanation: Made it complex by adding the subordinate clause "because she helped the poor," which provides a reason for the main clause.

(g) What a passionate woman Mother Teresa was!
Explanation: Converted to an exclamatory sentence using the "What a..." structure to express strong feeling.

(h) She helped the helpless.
Explanation: Simplified to a single independent clause by removing the relative clause, making it a simple sentence.

(i) She set up "Nirmal Hridoy" in Kolkata, and it served the needy.
Explanation: Created a compound sentence by joining two independent clauses with "and".

(j) Everyone knows about Mother Teresa's charity.
Explanation: Changed the interrogative into an assertive (declarative) sentence that states the fact directly.

Question #322 (ID: 481321)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) We are grateful to the freedom fighters. (Make it negative sentence)

(b) Their contribution is greater than any other thing. (Make it positive Degree)

(c) The freedom fighters who died in the Liberation War are called martyrs. (Make it a compound sentence)

(d) The National memorial has been built with a view to paying tribute to their memories. (Make it complex sentence)

(e) A freedom fighter is the greatest son of the soil. (Make it comparative sentence)

(f) They fought bravely and snatched the red sun of independence. (Make it simple sentence)

(g) Mother Teresa was a very passionate woman. (Make it an exclamatory sentence)

(h) Though their weapons were ordinary, they had much conrage in their mind. (Make it compound sentence)

(i) Their contribution will never be forgotten. (Affirmative sentence)

(j) The government has taken some steps to improve the condition. (Passive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) We are not ungrateful to the freedom fighters.

(b) No other thing is so/as great as their contribution.

(c) The freedom fighters died in the Liberation War and are called martyrs.

(d) The National Memorial has been built so that we can pay tribute to their memories.

(e) A freedom fighter is greater than any other son of the soil.

(f) Didn't we get our independence for their sacrifice?

(g) Fighting bravely, they snatched the red sun of independence.

(h) Their weapons were ordinary, but they had much courage in their mind.

(i) Their contribution will always/ever be remembered.

(j) Some steps to improve their condition have been taken by the government.

or, Some steps have been taken by the government to improve their condition.

Explanation:
(a) "We are not grateful to the freedom fighters."  
Explanation: This is the negative form of the affirmative sentence; adding "not" after the verb "are" makes the sentence negative.

(b) "No other thing is as great as their contribution."  
Explanation: To change a superlative/comparative into the positive degree we use the structure "as + adjective + as"; this shows equality in positive form.

(c) "Some freedom fighters died in the Liberation War, and they are called martyrs."  
Explanation: A compound sentence joins two independent clauses ("Some freedom fighters died..." and "they are called martyrs") with a coordinating conjunction "and."

(d) "The National Memorial has been built so that people may pay tribute to their memories."  
Explanation: This is a complex sentence because it has a main clause and a subordinate purpose clause ("so that...") showing why the memorial was built.

(e) "A freedom fighter is greater than any other son of the soil."  
Explanation: A comparative sentence uses "greater than" to compare one thing with others, replacing the superlative "greatest."

(f) "They fought bravely and snatched the red sun of independence."  
Explanation: This is a simple sentence with one subject "They" and a compound predicate ("fought... and snatched..."), so it remains simple.

(g) "What a passionate woman Mother Teresa was!"  
Explanation: An exclamatory sentence expresses strong feeling; beginning with "What" and reordering the clause makes it exclamatory.

(h) "Their weapons were ordinary, but they had much courage in their minds."  
Explanation: Turning the subordinate contrast into two independent clauses joined by "but" makes it a compound sentence that shows contrast.

(i) "People will always remember their contribution."  
Explanation: To make the sentence affirmative, remove the negation "never" and use a positive adverb "always," here with an active subject "People."

(j) "Some steps have been taken by the government to improve the condition."  
Explanation: Converting the active sentence to passive makes the object "some steps" the subject and uses the correct tense form "have been taken" to match present perfect.

Question #323 (ID: 481322)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) We should read books to gain knowledge. (Make it a complex sentence)

(b) Books introduce us to the realm of knowledge. (Make it passive)

(c) The books of great writers contain noble thoughts and great ideas. (Make it an interrogative sentence)

(d) If we read books, we can enrich our minds. (Make it a simple sentence)

(e) Books are the greatest friends. (Make it positive)

(f) They give us both knowledge and pleasure. (Make it Negative)

(g) As they are our real friends, they remain with us in time of danger. (Make it a compound sentence)

(h) Some books are very interesting. (Make it an exclamatory sentence)

(i) We can build up a developed society by reading books. (Make it a complex sentence)

(j) Nothing but books can remove the darkness of ignorance. (Make it an affirmative sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) We should read books so that we can gain knowledge.

(b) We are introduced to the realm of knowledge by books.

(c) Don't the books of great writers contain noble thoughts and great ideas?

(d) By reading books, we can enrich our mind.

(e) No other friend is so great as books.

(f) They give us not only knowledge but also pleasure.

(g) They are our real friends and so they remain with us in time of danger.

(h) How interesting some books are!

(i) If we read books, we can build up a developed society.

(j) Only books can remove the darkness of ignorance.

Explanation:
(a) We should read books because they help us gain knowledge.
Explanation: Using "because" joins an independent clause and a subordinate clause, so the sentence becomes complex and shows reason.

(b) We are introduced to the realm of knowledge by books.
Explanation: The object "us" becomes the subject and the doer "books" is placed after "by", forming the passive voice.

(c) Do the books of great writers contain noble thoughts and great ideas?
Explanation: For present simple questions we add the auxiliary "do" before the subject to form an interrogative sentence.

(d) Reading books enriches our minds.
Explanation: This is a single independent clause with a gerund subject, so it is a simple sentence expressing one complete idea.

(e) Books are great friends.
Explanation: Replacing the superlative "greatest" with the positive degree "great" produces the positive form.

(f) They do not give us either knowledge or pleasure.
Explanation: To make a negative of "both ... and" we use "do not" plus "either ... or" to negate the two items.

(g) They are our real friends, and they remain with us in time of danger.
Explanation: Two independent clauses are joined with the coordinating conjunction "and," making the sentence compound.

(h) How interesting some books are!
Explanation: Using "How" + adjective + subject + verb forms an exclamatory sentence showing strong feeling.

(i) If we read books, we can build up a developed society.
Explanation: Beginning with "if" creates a subordinate (conditional) clause plus a main clause, so the sentence becomes complex.

(j) Only books can remove the darkness of ignorance.
Explanation: Replacing the negative phrase "Nothing but" with the affirmative limiter "Only" produces an affirmative sentence.

Question #324 (ID: 481323)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) There was an old man in a village. (Interrogative) (b) He was very poor but honest. (Complex) (c) He was one of the best cap makers with palm leaves. (Positive) (d) He sold them in the neighbouring market. (Voice change) (e) Earning money in this way, he thus maintained his family. (Compound) (f) One day he could not but go to a market. (Affirmative) (g) The market was far from his house. (Negative) (h) He had a basket full of caps. (Complex) (i) He was too tired to walk. (Compound) (j) He sat under the tree and fell asleep. (Simple)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Wasn't there an old man in a village?

(b) Though he was very poor, he was honest.

(c) Very few cap makers with palm leaves were so/as good as he.

(d) They were sold in the neighbouring market by him.

(e) He earned money in this way and thus maintained his family.

(f) One day he had to go to a market.

(g) The market was not near his house.

(h) He had a basket which was full of caps.

(i) He was very tired and could not walk.

(j) Sitting under the tree, he fell asleep.

Explanation:
(a) Was there an old man in the village? — Change to a question by inverting the auxiliary verb "was" before the subject; "There was..." becomes "Was there...?" to form an interrogative.

(b) Though he was very poor, he was honest. — This is complex because a subordinate clause ("Though he was very poor") is joined to the main clause to show contrast, so one clause depends on the other.

(c) He was a good cap maker with palm leaves. — "One of the best" is a superlative; the positive degree replaces it with "good" to state the quality without comparison.

(d) They were sold by him in the neighbouring market. — Passive voice makes the object ("them") the subject and uses the appropriate auxiliary + past participle, with the agent added by "by him."

(e) He earned money in this way, and thus he maintained his family. — Two independent clauses ("He earned..." and "he maintained...") are joined with the coordinating conjunction "and," making a compound sentence.

(f) One day he had to go to a market. — "Could not but go" is a negative idiom meaning necessity; the affirmative equivalent is "had to go," keeping the same meaning in positive form.

(g) The market was not near his house. — To make it negative, negate the statement by inserting "not" and restating the idea in opposite terms while keeping tense and subject.

(h) He had a basket that was full of caps. — A relative clause ("that was full of caps") modifies "basket," creating a complex sentence with a main clause plus a dependent clause.

(i) He was too tired, so he could not walk. — Two related independent clauses expressing cause and effect are joined by "so," forming a compound sentence.

(j) He sat under the tree and fell asleep. — This is a simple sentence because it has one subject ("He") with a compound predicate ("sat... and fell asleep"), so it remains a single independent clause.

Question #325 (ID: 481324)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Strategy is the most important thing in the examination. (Comparative)

(b) Any answer in the exam should not be elaborated. (Active)

(c) When he gets the question paper he should read it carefully. (Simple)

(d) At first glance, the questions may seem difficult. (Negative)

(e) A student should attempt to answer all the questions to get good marks. (Complex)

(f) If an examinee answers all the questions, the examiner becomes glad to see that. (Simple)

(g) But, it is better than not answering at all. (Positive)

(h) It is really sensible. (Exclamatory)

(i)The examinee should not waste time by doing it. (Passive)

(j) Without following this process, you cannot bring a good result in an examination. (Compound)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Strategy is more important than any other thing (or, all other things) in the examination.

(b) The examinees/The students should not elaborate any answer in the examination.

(c) After getting/Getting the question paper, he should read it carefully.

(d) At first glance, the questions may not seem easy.

(e) A student should attempt to answer all the questions so that s/he can/may get good marks.

(f) Seeing answering all the question by an examinee, the examiner become glad.

(g) But not answering at all is not as/so good as it.

(h) How sensible it is!

(i) Time by doing it should not be wasted by the examinee.

(j) Follow this process or you cannot bring a good result in an examination.

Explanation:
(a) The label “Comparative” is incorrect; the sentence uses the superlative phrase “most important,” so it is a superlative statement, not comparative—comparative would use “more important.”

(b) The label “Active” is incorrect; “should not be elaborated” is passive voice (modal + past participle). An active form would be “You should not elaborate any answer.”

(c) This is a complex sentence because it has a subordinate adverbial clause “When he gets the question paper” plus the main clause “he should read it carefully,” so there are two clauses with a dependent–independent relationship.

(d) The label “Negative” is wrong; the sentence is affirmative (positive) in meaning—“may seem difficult” expresses a possibility, not a negation.

(e) The label “Complex” is incorrect; this is a simple sentence with one finite verb phrase “should attempt” and an infinitive phrase of purpose “to get good marks,” so it contains only one independent clause.

(f) The label “Simple” is incorrect; this is a complex sentence because it begins with the conditional subordinate clause “If an examinee answers all the questions” followed by the main clause “the examiner becomes glad to see that.”

(g) The label “Positive” is acceptable: the sentence is affirmative (not negative). Although it contains a comparative “better than,” it is a positive/affirmative statement rather than a negative one.

(h) The label “Exclamatory” is incorrect; the sentence is a plain declarative statement (“It is really sensible”), not formed or punctuated as an exclamation.

(i) The label “Passive” is incorrect; this is an active sentence with a modal verb (“should not waste”) where the subject “The examinee” performs the action—passive would be “Time should not be wasted by the examinee.”

(j) The label “Compound” is incorrect; the sentence is simple: it has one independent clause “you cannot bring a good result in an examination” with a prepositional/participial phrase “Without following this process” serving as an adverbial modifier, not a second independent clause.

Question #326 (ID: 481325)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Haji Mohammod Mohsin was more generous than any other man in this subcontinents. (Positive)

(b) He was born in Hoogly. (complex)

(c) He inherited a vast property from his father and sister. (Interrogative)

(d) He did not misuse this wealth. (Passive)

(e)He is called a friend of humanity. (Active)

(f) He didn’t marry. (Affirmative)

(g) During his life time, he spent money lavishly to help the poor. (Compound)

(h) He was very kind to the poor. (Negative)

(i) One night when he was saying his prayer, a theif broke into his room. (Simple)

(j) He caught the thief but didn’t punish him. (Complex)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) No other man in this subcontinent was so/as generous as Haji Muhammad Mohsin.

(b) It is Hoogly where he was born. / Hoogly is the place where he was born.

(c) Didn't he inherit a vast property from his father and sister?

or. Did he not inherit a vast property from his father and sister?

(d) This wealth was not misused by him.

(e) People/We call him a friend of humanity.

(f) He was unmarried.

Or, He was a bachelor.

Or. He was single.

(g) During his lifetime, he spent money lavishly and helped the poor.

Or, He wanted to help the poor and so he spent money lavishly during his life time.

(h) He was not at all cruel/unkind to the poor.

(i) One night, at the time of his saying prayer, a thief broke into his room.

Or, One night during his prayer, a thief broke into his room.

(j) Though/Although he caught the thief, he did not punish him.

Explanation:
a Correct classification: Superlative. The sentence compares him with every other man ("more ... than any other"), which expresses the highest degree; the positive degree would be just "generous" without comparison.

b Correct classification: Simple sentence. It has a single independent clause ("He was born in Hoogly") with no subordinate clause or coordinated clause, so it is simple rather than complex.

c Correct classification: Declarative (statement). The sentence states a fact; an interrogative would be formed as "Did he inherit a vast property...?" so the given form is not a question.

d Correct classification: Active (negative). The subject "He" performs the action ("did not misuse"), so it is active voice with negation; the passive would be "This wealth was not misused by him."

e Correct classification: Passive. "He is called a friend of humanity" shows the subject receiving the action (being called), so it is passive, not active.

f Correct classification: Negative. "He didn't marry" contains negation ("didn't"), so it is a negative sentence; the affirmative form would be "He married."

g Correct classification: Simple sentence. It contains one main clause with adverbials ("During his life time, he spent...") and no second independent clause, so it is not compound.

h Correct classification: Affirmative. "He was very kind to the poor" affirms a quality and contains no negation, so it is affirmative, not negative.

i Correct classification: Complex sentence. It has a main clause ("a thief broke into his room") plus a subordinate time clause ("when he was saying his prayer"), so it is complex.

j Correct classification: Compound sentence. It joins two independent clauses ("He caught the thief" and "didn’t punish him") with the conjunction "but," so it is compound rather than complex.
