Question #327 (ID: 481326)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Who does not want to succeed in life? (Assertive)

(b) It is not an easy thing. (Affirmative)

(c) Being industrious, everyone can prosper in life. (Negative)

(d) The idle always lag behind. (complex)

(e) We must work hard so that we can earn money. (simple)

(f) By working hard, we can improve our lot. (compound)

(g) The light of prosperity can be seen by a hard working person. (Active)

(h) Women should work as much as men. (comparative)

(i) We should remember that industry is the key to success. (passive)

(j) An idle man leads a very miserable life. (Exclamatory)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Everybody wants to succeed in life.

Or, There is nobody but wants to succeed in life.

(b) It is a difficult thing.

(c) Without being industrious, no one can prosper in life.

Or, Being lazy/idle, none can prosper in life.

(d) Those who are idle, always lag behind.

(e) We must work hard to earn money.

(f) We will work hard and thus we can improve our lot.

(g) A hard-working person can see the light of prosperity.

(h) Women should not work less than men.

(i) It should be remembered by us that industry is the key to success.

Or, That industry is the key to success should be remembered by us.

(j) What a miserable life an idle man leads!

Explanation:
(a) Who does not want to succeed in life? — This is an interrogative sentence because it asks a question beginning with the question word "Who", so it is not assertive.

(b) It is not an easy thing. — This is negative: the word "not" negates the statement, so it is not an affirmative sentence.

(c) Being industrious, everyone can prosper in life. — This is affirmative because the main clause ("everyone can prosper") affirms a positive possibility; the opening participle phrase does not make it negative.

(d) The idle always lag behind. — This is a simple declarative sentence with one subject and one predicate, so it is simple rather than complex.

(e) We must work hard so that we can earn money. — This is complex because it has a main clause ("We must work hard") plus a subordinate purpose clause ("so that we can earn money").

(f) By working hard, we can improve our lot. — This is a simple sentence: one main clause with an introductory participial phrase, not a compound (which would have two independent clauses).

(g) The light of prosperity can be seen by a hard working person. — This is passive voice because the subject ("the light of prosperity") receives the action and the agent appears in a "by" phrase; the active form would be "A hard-working person can see the light of prosperity."

(h) Women should work as much as men. — This is comparative (equality) because "as much as" compares the amount of work between women and men.

(i) We should remember that industry is the key to success. — This is active voice: the subject "we" performs the action "should remember"; it is not passive.

(j) An idle man leads a very miserable life. — This is a declarative/affirmative (assertive) sentence stating a fact; it is not exclamatory, which would express strong emotion or use an exclamation.

Question #328 (ID: 481327)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2017 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
how dare you are to wake me up the lion roared i shall kill you for that please let me go the mouse cried i did not mean to wake you up

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
"How daring you are to wake me up?" the lion roared. "I shall kill you for that." "Please, let me go." the mouse cried, "I did not mean to wake you up."

Explanation:
The correction is right because each spoken line is written as direct speech in quotation marks, begins with a capital letter, and ends with punctuation that matches the tone (an exclamation for anger, a period for a statement). When a speech tag follows in the same sentence, put a comma inside the closing quote before the tag (for example, "Please let me go," the mouse cried), but if the speech ends with an exclamation or question mark the strong punctuation stays inside the quotes and the tag is lowercased (for example, "How dare you wake me up!" the lion roared). These punctuation rules make it clear who is speaking and preserve the intended emotion.

Question #329 (ID: 481328)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) We should read books to acquire knowledge. (Make complex sentence)

(b) Books introduce us to the realm of knowledge. (Use passive voice)

(c) The books of great writers contain noble thoughts and great ideas. (Make interrogative sentence)

(d) By reading good books, we can enrich our mind. (Make compound sentence)

(e) Reading books is a very good habit. (Make exclamatory sentence)

(f) This habit is rarely disliked. (Affirmative)

(g) More and more books should be read. (Use active voice)

(h) No other thing is as interesting as reading books. (Use comparative degree)

(i) When we read good books, we discover new worlds. (Make simple sentence)

(f) Very few friends are as great as a good book. (Make superlative degree)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) We should read books so that we can acquire knowledge.

(b) We are introduced to the realm of knowledge by books.

(c) Don't the books of great writers contain noble thoughts and great ideas?

(d) We read books and we can enrich our mind.

(e) What a good habit reading books is!

(f) This habit is always/mostly/commonly/often liked.

(g) We should read more and more books.

(h) Reading books is more interesting than any other thing/anything.

(i) By reading good books, we discover new worlds.

Or. At the time of reading good books, we can discover new worlds.

(j) A good book is one of the greatest friends.

Explanation:
(a) We should read books so that we may acquire knowledge.  
This is a complex sentence because it has a main clause ("We should read books") and a subordinate purpose clause ("so that we may acquire knowledge").

(b) We are introduced to the realm of knowledge by books.  
Passive voice is formed with a form of "be" + past participle; the original object ("us"/"we") becomes the subject and "books" becomes the agent introduced by "by."

(c) Do the books of great writers contain noble thoughts and great ideas?  
To make it interrogative, place the auxiliary "do" before the subject ("the books") and keep the main verb in base form.

(d) By reading good books, we can enrich our mind, and we can broaden our knowledge.  
This is a compound sentence because it joins two independent clauses ("we can enrich our mind" and "we can broaden our knowledge") with the coordinating conjunction "and."

(e) What a very good habit reading books is!  
An exclamatory sentence uses "What..." (or "How...") to show strong feeling and inverts the usual order for emphasis.

(f) Most people like this habit.  
To make it affirmative, express the idea positively: "rarely disliked" becomes "liked by most people" (here phrased as "Most people like this habit").

(g) People should read more and more books.  
Active voice makes the doer ("People") the subject who performs the action, instead of the passive "books should be read."

(h) Reading books is more interesting than anything else.  
Use the comparative form "more ... than" to compare reading books with other things.

(i) Reading good books opens up new worlds.  
A simple sentence has a single independent clause; here "Reading good books" is the subject and "opens up new worlds" is the predicate.

(f) A good book is the best of friends.  
To form the superlative, use "best" to show the highest degree, replacing the comparative idea "as great as."

Question #330 (ID: 481329)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Once upon a time two friends were passing by a forest. (Make it complex sentence)

(b) They were talking about their love for each other. (Make it interrogative meaning)

(c) Suddenly they saw a bear which was coming towards them. (Make it simple sentence)

(d) The first friend climbed up a tree. (Make it a complex sentence)

(e) The later could not climb up a tree. (Make it an affirmative sentence)

(f) He did not find any way. (Make it a passive voice)

(g) He lay down on the ground and feigned death. (Make it a simple sentence)

(h) The bear smelt his ears, nose and face. (Use passive voice)

(i) He was thought to be dead. (Make it a complex sentence)

(j) The bear went away and he escaped himself. (Make it a complex sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Once upon a time, there were two friends who were passing by a forest.

(b) Weren't they talking about their love for each other?"

(c) Suddenly they saw a bear coming towards them.

(d) It was the first friend who climbed up a tree.

(e) The latter was unable to climb up a tree.

(f) No way was found by him.

(g) Lying down on the ground, he feigned death.

(h) His ears, nose and face were smelt by the bear.

(i) He was thought that he was dead/The bear thought that he was dead/It was he who was thought to be dead.

(j) When the bear went away, he escaped himself.

Explanation:
(a) Complex sentence: Once upon a time, two friends were passing by a forest when they heard a rustling sound.
Explanation: This is complex because it has an independent clause ("two friends were passing by a forest") and a dependent time clause introduced by "when"; the dependent clause adds extra information and makes the sentence complex.

(b) Interrogative: Were they talking about their love for each other?
Explanation: Forming a question requires inversion of the auxiliary verb and the subject ("Were" + "they"), which turns the statement into an interrogative.

(c) Simple sentence: Suddenly, they saw a bear approaching.
Explanation: The simple sentence contains a single main clause with one verb phrase ("saw a bear approaching"); removing the relative clause makes it one independent clause.

(d) Complex sentence: When the bear appeared, the first friend climbed up a tree.
Explanation: This is complex because it joins a subordinate time clause ("When the bear appeared") to the main clause, so there is a dependent clause plus an independent clause.

(e) Affirmative sentence: The latter failed to climb up the tree.
Explanation: This affirmative form conveys the same idea without using "not" by using a positive verb ("failed") to express inability.

(f) Passive voice: No way was found by him.
Explanation: In passive voice the object ("no way") becomes the subject and the verb uses a form of "to be" + past participle ("was found"), with the agent optionally added ("by him").

(g) Simple sentence: He lay on the ground, feigning death.
Explanation: Using the participle phrase "feigning death" attaches information to the main clause without adding another clause, so the sentence remains one simple clause.

(h) Passive voice: His ears, nose, and face were smelled by the bear.
Explanation: The object(s) ("his ears, nose, and face") become the subject of the passive clause, followed by "were" + past participle ("smelled"), and the agent is introduced with "by the bear."

(i) Complex sentence: Because he lay motionless, people thought that he was dead.
Explanation: This is complex because it contains a subordinate reason clause ("Because he lay motionless") plus the main clause; the subordinate clause explains why the main clause happened.

(j) Complex sentence: After the bear went away, he escaped.
Explanation: The time clause "After the bear went away" is a dependent clause joined to the main clause "he escaped," making the sentence complex.

Question #331 (ID: 481330)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) William Wordsworth is one of the best well-known poets in English literature (Positive).

(b) He was the second of his father’s five sons (Negative).

(c) He was born at Cumberland on April 4, 1770 (Complex).

(d) When he was eight years old, his mother died (Simple).

(e) At the same year he was sent to the Grammar School of Hawkshead for education (Compound).

(f) He was only 13 years old when his father died (Interrogative).

(g) Fundamental education had been given to him at the school (Active).

(h) The education that he learnt from this institution played better role in his life (Simple).

(i) The readers called for a new edition of his famous book “The Lyrical Ballads” in 1800 (Passive).

(j) This book brought a huge name and fame in his life (Exclamatory).

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Very few well-known poets in English literature are as/so good as William Wordsworth.

(b) Wasn't he the second of his father's five sons?

Or. He was none but the second of his father's five sons.

(c) Cumberland was the place where he was born on April 4, 1770.

Or, He was born in Cumberland when it was April 4, 1770.

Or, When it was April 4, 1770, he was born in Cumberland.

(d) His mother died at his eight years old.

Or. At his eight years old his mother died.

(e) In the same year he was sent to the Grammar School of Hawkshead and he was educated there.

(f) Wasn't he only 13 years old when his father died?

(g) The teachers had given him fundamental education at the school.

(h) The education learnt from this institution played better role in his life.

(i) A new edition of his famous book, "The Lyrical Ballads" was called for by the readers in 1800.

(j) What a name and fame this book brought in his life!

Explanation:
Explanation:

a Correctly called “Positive” because it is an affirmative (declarative) sentence stating a fact about Wordsworth without any negation or question.

b This is not a negative sentence; it is an affirmative declarative stating a fact. A negative sentence would include words like “not” or other negators.

c The sentence is not complex; it is a simple declarative with a time phrase [math]“on April 4, 1770”[/math] rather than a subordinate clause. A complex sentence needs a dependent clause with its own subject and verb.

d This is actually complex, not simple, because it begins with the subordinate clause [math]“When he was eight years old”[/math] (it has its own subject and verb) followed by the main clause “his mother died.”

e This is not compound but a simple sentence: it contains a single independent clause describing an action in that year, with no second independent clause joined by a conjunction.

f It is not interrogative; it is a declarative sentence. It is complex because the phrase [math]“when his father died”[/math] is a subordinate clause attached to the main clause.

g This sentence is passive (the action is received: “had been given to him”); the active form would be “The school had given him fundamental education.” Therefore labeling it “Active” is incorrect.

h This is complex, not simple, because it contains a relative (dependent) clause [math]“that he learnt from this institution”[/math] modifying “The education,” so there is more than one clause.

i The sentence is active: “The readers” is the subject performing the action “called for.” The passive version would be “A new edition was called for by the readers,” so labeling it “Passive” is wrong.

j This is a declarative sentence, not exclamatory; an exclamatory sentence would show strong emotion and typically use an exclamation form (e.g., “What a famous book this was!”).

Question #332 (ID: 481331)

Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Mr. Rahim, one of my cousins is a good teacher. (Complex)

(b) He is older than I. (Positive degree)

(c) He wants his students to be good citizen. (Complex)

(d) He leaves no stone unturned to teach them morality. (Affirmative)

(e) He becomes very happy when the students achieve good results in public examinations. (Exclamatory)

(f) Mr. Rahim is not only punctual but also sincere. (Simple)

(g) He is the best teacher in our area. (Negative)

(h) He cannot remain sitting in the class. (Affirmative)

(i) He goes to class after taking preparation. (Compound)

(j) All the students respect him very much. (Passive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Mr. Rahim, who is a good teacher, is one of my cousins.

Or, Mr. Rahim, who is one of my cousins, is a good teacher.

or, Mr. Rahim is a good teacher who is one of my cousins.

(b) I am not as old as he.

(c) He wants that his students will/may/should be good citizens.

(d) He tries his best to teach them morality.

(e) How happy he becomes when the students achieve good results in public examinations!

(f) Besides being punctual Mr. Rahim is sincere.

(g) No other teacher in our area is so/as good as he.

(h) He is unable to remain sitting in the class.

or, Can he remain sitting in the class?.

(i) He takes preparation and goes to class.

(j) He is very much respected by all the students.

Explanation:
(a) This is a simple sentence with an appositive phrase "one of my cousins" giving extra information about the subject; there is only one finite verb ("is"), so it's simple.

(b) "Older" is the comparative degree of "old" used to compare two people, so the sentence shows a comparative degree.

(c) This is a simple sentence: one main clause ("He wants") with an object phrase ("his students to be good citizens"); the infinitive phrase does not make a separate clause.

(d) It is affirmative because it states a positive action (he tries very hard); there is no negation.

(e) This is a complex sentence: it has a main clause ("He becomes very happy") and a subordinate adverbial clause introduced by "when" ("when the students achieve good results"), so there are two parts with different roles.

(f) It is simple: one subject and one finite verb ("is"), with two linked adjectives joined by the correlative pair "not only... but also," so still a single clause.

(g) "Best" is the superlative degree of "good/good," showing the highest degree among more than two, so the sentence expresses a superlative.

(h) This is negative because it contains the negative auxiliary "cannot," indicating inability or impossibility.

(i) It is a complex sentence because the main action ("He goes to class") is followed by a subordinate time/condition phrase ("after taking preparation"), forming a main clause plus a subordinate element.

(j) The sentence is active voice: the subject ("All the students") performs the action ("respect him"); the passive form would be "He is respected by all the students."

Question #333 (ID: 481332)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Is there anybody who does not want to succeed in life? (Assertive)

(b) Do you know it? (Passive)

(c) An industrious man will shine in life. (Complex)

(d) Hard work is needed for success. (Active)

(e) A life with an assignment is an actual life. (Negative)

(f) No one can receive any reward unless he works hard. (Simple)

(g) One can’t be successful without it. (Interrogative)

(h) A successful man is very happy. (Exclamatory)

(i) No other man is as happy as a successful man. (Superlative)

(j) A hardworking man is healthier than an idle man. (Positive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Everybody wants to succeed in life.

(b) Is it known to you?

(c) A man who is industrious will shine in life.

(d) We need hard work for success.

(e) A life without an assignment is not an actual life.

(f) No one can receive any reward without working hard.

(g) Can one be successful without it?

(h) How happy a successful man is!

(i) A successful man is the happiest man.

(j) An idle man is not so healthy as a hard-working man.

Explanation:
(a) Assertive: "Everyone wants to succeed in life."  
Reason: An interrogative asking if anybody does not want success is best turned into a universal affirmative by stating the general truth — "everyone" — as the assertive form.

(b) Passive: "Is it known to you?"  
Reason: To make passive, the object "it" becomes the subject and the verb changes to passive form "is known," with "to you" indicating the agent/recipient.

(c) Complex: "If a man is industrious, he will shine in life."  
Reason: A complex sentence has a main clause plus a subordinate clause; using an "if" conditional links cause (being industrious) to result (shining in life), forming a complex sentence.

(d) Active: "One must work hard to succeed."  
Reason: Change the impersonal passive "is needed" into an active verb with an explicit subject ("one") so the doer performs the action in the active voice.

(e) Negative: "A life without an assignment is not an actual life."  
Reason: Negation is formed by replacing "with" by "without" and adding "not" to deny the original affirmative statement.

(f) Simple: "Hard work is necessary for any reward."  
Reason: A simple sentence states the idea directly without subordinate clauses; replacing "No one can receive… unless…" by a single-clause statement expresses the same necessity simply.

(g) Interrogative: "Can one be successful without it?"  
Reason: To form a question, invert the modal auxiliary "can" and the subject "one" so the sentence becomes interrogative.

(h) Exclamatory: "How happy a successful man is!"  
Reason: Exclamatory sentences use "how" (or "what") plus an adjective/noun to express strong feeling, turning a plain statement into an exclamation.

(i) Superlative: "A successful man is the happiest of all."  
Reason: The superlative uses "the" + adjective + "-est" (or "most") to show the highest degree; "of all" emphasizes comparison with everyone else.

(j) Positive: "A hardworking man is healthy; an idle man is not."  
Reason: The positive degree states qualities without comparison by using the base adjective ("healthy") and, if contrast is needed, the opposite form for the other subject.

Question #334 (ID: 481333)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Sylhet Board | Tags: Sylhet Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Long time ago, there lived a young man called Ruplal. (Make compound sentence)

(b) He lived with his family and worked on a farm. (Make interrogative sentence)

(c) It was a beautiful place but there were a lot a problems (Make complex sentence)

(d) The village people were quarrelsome. (Make negative sentence)

(e) Ruplal decided to go and live alone in the jungle in order to find peace. (Make complex sentence)

(f) So he collected his things and went to live by himself. (Make simple sentence)

(g) Ruplal made a nice little hut for himself in the jungle (Use passive voice)

(h) How happy I am now! (Make assertive sentence)

(i) My jungle hut is one of the most peaceful places in the world. (Make positive degree)

(j) That night, while Ruplal was sleeping, he heard a noise. (Make simple sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Long time ago, there lived a young man and his name was Ruplal,

(b) Didn't he live with his family and work on a farm?

(c) Though it was a beautiful place, there were a lot of problems.

(d) The village people were not peace-loving.

(e) Ruplal decided to go and live alone in the jungle so that he could find peace.

(f) So collecting his things, he went to live by himself.

(g) A nice little hut was made for himself by Ruplal.

(h) I am very happy now.

(i) Very few places in the world are so/as peaceful as my jungle hut.

(j) During sleeping that night, Ruplal heard a noise.

Or, At the time of sleeping that night, Ruplal heard a noise.

Explanation:
Explanation:

a A long time ago there lived a young man called Ruplal, and he led a simple life.  
This is a compound sentence because it joins two independent clauses with the coordinating conjunction "and."

b Did he live with his family and work on a farm?  
This is a yes/no interrogative formed by using the auxiliary "did" and the base form of the verbs.

c Although it was a beautiful place, there were a lot of problems.  
This is a complex sentence because "Although..." introduces a subordinate clause that contrasts with the main clause, so one clause depends on the other.

d The village people were not quarrelsome.  
The negative is formed by inserting "not" after the auxiliary verb "were."

e Ruplal decided to go and live alone in the jungle so that he could find peace.  
This is complex because "so that..." introduces a dependent clause of purpose, explaining why he decided to go.

f Collecting his things, he went to live by himself.  
This is a simple sentence with a single main clause; the participial phrase "Collecting his things" modifies the subject but does not create a second clause.

g A nice little hut was made by Ruplal in the jungle.  
This is the passive voice: the object of the active sentence becomes the subject, and the verb becomes the appropriate form of "to be" + past participle.

h I am very happy now.  
This assertive (declarative) sentence states the speaker’s feeling as a fact rather than exclaiming it.

i My jungle hut is peaceful.  
This uses the positive degree of the adjective "peaceful" (the base form) instead of the superlative "one of the most peaceful."

j That night he heard a noise.  
This is a simple sentence because it has a single main clause expressing one complete idea.

Question #336 (ID: 481335)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Corruption is one of the worst evils. (Positive)

(b) A corrupted man can do anything against morality. (Complex)

(c) People hate a corrupted man. (Passive)

(d) Nobody respects him. (Interrogative)

(e) The man who takes bribe is next to devil. (Simple)

(f) Though we have strick law, we are still affected by this evil. (Compound)

(g) No other person is as hated as a corrupted man. (Superlative)

(h) We hope that Bangladesh will be free from this evil. (Simple)

(i) Everybody avoids a corrupted man. (Negative)

(j) A corrupted man leads a very unhappy life. (Exclamatory)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Very few evils are so bad as corruption.

(b) A corrupt man can do anything which is against morality.

Or. A man, who is corrupt, can do anything against morality.

(c) A corrupt man is hated by people.

(d) Does anybody respect him?

Or. Who respects him?

(e) The man taking bribe is next to devil.

(f) We have strict law, but we are affected by this evil.

(g) A corrupt man is the most hated person.

(h) We hope Bangladesh to be free from this evil.

(i) There is nobody but avoids a corrupt man.

Or. Nobody mixes with a corrupt man.

Or. There is nobody who does not avoid a corrupt man.

(j) What an unhappy life a corrupt man leads!

Explanation:
a This is a positive (affirmative) sentence because it states a fact/opinion directly without any negation or question; it affirms that corruption is among the worst evils.

b It is called complex because the main idea ("A corrupted man can do anything") is expanded by an additional clause/phrase ("against morality") that describes manner and tightens the meaning; a complex sentence mixes a main clause with subordinate information to give fuller detail.

c The label “passive” applies when the object becomes the subject, e.g. the passive form is "A corrupted man is hated by people"; passive voice is formed with an appropriate form of "be" + past participle to show the action is received.

d An interrogative asks a question; to make this sentence interrogative we invert the auxiliary: "Does nobody respect him?" or more naturally "Does anyone respect him?"; the sentence form changes to request information rather than state a fact.

e It’s treated as simple here because it expresses one main idea with a single finite verb ("is"); though it contains a relative phrase ("who takes bribe") that describes the subject, the sentence conveys one complete thought centered on "is next to devil."

f It’s labeled compound because it shows two contrasted clauses joined by a conjunction and expressing related ideas: one clause states a condition ("Though we have strict law") and the other states the result/contrast ("we are still affected by this evil"); such coordination or linking of clauses yields a compound/complex sense that contrasts two equal points.

g This is marked superlative because it expresses the highest degree of hatred by comparing everyone else to the corrupted man ("No other person is as hated as a corrupted man"), effectively singling him out as most hated.

h It’s classed simple because it conveys a single straightforward thought ("We hope") with a clear object clause; the sentence is a single declarative statement expressing a hope about Bangladesh’s future.

i It’s considered negative in sense because it indicates refusal of association—people do not associate with him ("everybody avoids him"), so the sentence expresses a negative social response even though grammatically it uses an affirmative verb.

j The exclamatory label applies when the idea is expressed with strong feeling, e.g. as an exclamation: "What an unhappy life a corrupted man leads!"—such a form uses exclamatory structure or punctuation to show strong emotion.

Question #337 (ID: 481336)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2016 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Bangladesh is a low-lying country. (Make interrogative)

(b) Every year natural disasters visiť us. (Make passive voice)

(c) Flood is one of the most dangerous natural disasters. (Use comparative degree)

(d) It is Dhaka city which has not yet suffered any severe earthquake. (Make simple sentence)

(e) The people living in the high land can escape flood. (Make complex sentence)

(f) Crops are damaged by this flood. (Make active voice)

(g) Who does not know the consequence of 'Tsunami'? (Make assertive sentence)

(h) The recent flood was very devastating. (Make exclamatory sentence)

(i) Bangladesh is in the active earthquake zone. (Make negative)

(j) Dhaka is the most risky city in the earthquake zone. (Use positive degree)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Isn't Bangladesh a low-lying country?

(b) We are visited by natural disasters every year.

(c) Flood is more dangerous than most other natural disasters.

(d) Dhaka city has not yet suffered any severe earthquake.

(e) The people who live in the high land, can escape flood.

Or. It is the people who live in the high land can escape flood.

Or. There are people who tive in the high land can escape flood.

(f) This flood damages crops.

(g) Everybody knows the consequences of Tsunami.

(h) How devastating the recent flood was!

(i) Bangladesh is not in the inactive earthquake zone.

(j) No other city in the earthquake zone is so/as risky as Dhaka.

Explanation:
(a) Is Bangladesh a low-lying country?
This is a yes/no question formed by inverting the subject and the auxiliary verb "is" because the original sentence has no auxiliary.

(b) We are visited by natural disasters every year.
In passive voice the object ("us") becomes the subject ("we"), the original subject becomes the agent introduced by "by," and the tense (simple present) is kept with "are visited."

(c) Floods are more dangerous than many other natural disasters.
To make a comparative, use "more + adjective + than" to compare floods with other natural disasters; here "more dangerous than" replaces the superlative phrase.

(d) Dhaka city has not yet suffered any severe earthquake.
Remove the cleft structure "It is ... which" and put the real subject "Dhaka city" before the verb to make a simple sentence.

(e) The people who live on the high land can escape floods.
A complex sentence is formed by adding a subordinate relative clause "who live on the high land" describing "the people."

(f) This flood damages crops.
Convert to active voice by making the agent "this flood" the subject and changing the verb to the active form "damages."

(g) Everyone knows the consequences of a tsunami.
Change the interrogative into a declarative (assertive) sentence; "everyone knows" states the idea positively.

(h) What a devastating flood the recent one was!
Use an exclamatory structure with "What" + noun phrase (or "How" + adjective) and invert the subject and verb to show strong feeling.

(i) Bangladesh is not in the active earthquake zone.
Form the negative by inserting "not" after the auxiliary verb "is."

(j) Dhaka is a risky city in the earthquake zone.
Use the positive (base) form of the adjective "risky" instead of the superlative "most risky" to state the quality without comparison.

Question #338 (ID: 481337)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Dhaka Board | Tags: Dhaka Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Television is one of the most wonderful inventions of modern science. (Positive)

(b) It was not invented over night. (Active)

(c) Scientists spent many years and worked hard to invent television. (complex)

(d) Nowadays, almost every family has a television set. (Negative)

(e) People of all ages like to watch television. (Interrogative)

(f) The programmes telecast by television are very interesting. ( Complex)

(g) Television should telecast educative programmes. (Passive)

(h) If you watch television, you can learn many things. (simple)

(i) People spend their free time by watching television. (Compound)

(j) Very few things are so useful as television. ( Superlative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Very few inventions of modern science are so/as wonderful as televisiori.

(b) Scientists/People/Inventors didn't invent it overnight.

(c) Scientists invented television after they had spent many years and worked hard.

Or. Scientists spent many years and worked hard so that they could invent television.

(d) Nowadays there is hardly any family that does not have a television set.

Or, Nowadays there is almost no family without having a television set.

(e) Don't people of all ages like to watch television?

(f) The programmes which are telecast by television are very interesting.

(g) Educative programmes should be telecast on television.

(h) By watching television, you can learn many things.

(i) People watch television and thus spend their free time.

(j) Television is one of the most useful things.

Explanation:
ক বাক্যটি ইতিবাচক (affirmative), কারণ এতে কোনো নেতিবাচক পদ নেই এবং বক্তব্য সরাসরি একটি সত্য স্থাপনা করেছে: টেলিভিশন আধুনিক বিজ্ঞানের একটি বিস্ময়কর আবিষ্কার।  

খ এটি নেতিবাচক ও বহুবচনীয় (passive) ধাঁচের বাক্য: "not" থাকার কারণে নেতিবাচক এবং কৃত্যটি বিষয় (it) কর্তৃক গ্রহণ করা হয়েছে, তাই passive voice।  

গ এখানে একক বিষয় ("Scientists") ও দুটো ক্রিয়া ("spent" এবং "worked") যুক্ত আছে, তাই এটি একটি simple sentence‑এর মতো একক স্বাধীন বাক্য যার compound predicate আছে।  

ঘ বাক্যটি ইতিবাচক (affirmative), কারণ এতে কোনো না-উপস্থিতি বা প্রশ্ন নেই — এটি সরাসরি জানাচ্ছে যে প্রায় প্রত্যেক পরিবারের টেলিভিশন আছে।  

ঙ এটি সাধারণ বিবৃতিমূলক (declarative) বাক্য, কারণ এটি কোনো প্রশ্ন করে না বা না-প্রকাশ করে; এটি কেবল একটি তথ্য দিচ্ছে যে সকল বয়সীদের মানুষদের টিভি দেখা ভালো লাগে।  

চ বাক্যটি সাধারণ সরল বাক্য যেখানে "telecast by television" একটি participle phrase হিসেবে "programmes" কে বর্ণনা করছে; বাক্যটির কাঠামো একটাই স্বাধীন ধারা, তাই এটি simple declarative।  

ছ বাক্যটি active voice—"Television" বিষয় হিসেবে কাজ করে এবং সরাসরি কর্মটি করছে ("should telecast"), তাই এটি passive নয় (passive হলে হবে: "Educative programmes should be telecast by television")।  

জ এটি একটি complex sentence কারণ এতে একটি শর্তসাপেক্ষ subordinate clause ("If you watch television") এবং একটি স্বাধীন মূল clause ("you can learn many things") আছে; শর্তাধীন clause একা দাঁড়াতে পারে না।  

ঝ বাক্যটি একটি সরল স্বাধীন বাক্য, একমাত্র স্বাধীন ধারা আছে যা বলছে মানুষ তাদের অবসর কিভাবে কাটায়; তাই এটি simple sentence।  

ঞ এটি তুলনামূলক (comparative) আকারে বক্তব্য করছে ("so useful as"), কারণ এটি টেলিভিশনকে অন্য কিছুর সঙ্গে তুলনা করছে; যদি superlative হতো তাহলে "the most useful" জাতীয় শব্দ ব্যবহার হতো।

Question #339 (ID: 481338)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Chittagong Board | Tags: Chattogram Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) My friend invited me to pay a visit to Cox’s Bazar. (complex)

(b) I was very glad. (negative)

(c) I accepted the invitation. (Passive)

(d) When I reached there, my friend received me cordially. (simple)

(e) I was excited to see the sea-beach. (Exlamatory)

(f) It is the largest sea-beach in the world. (Comparative)

(g) It is one of the most beautiful sea-beaches in the world. (Positive)

(h) It is called the pleasure seekers’ paradise. (Active)

(i) Every year a lot of people come to visit it. (Compound)

(j) If I could visit the sea-beach! (active)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) My friend invited me that/ in order that/ so that I could/might pay a visit to Cox's Bazar.

Or, It is my friend who invited me to pay a visit to Cox's Bazar.

Or, Cox's Bazar is the place where my friend invited me to visit.

(b) I was not (very) displeased/unhappy/sad at all.

Or, I could not but become glad.

(c) The invitation was accepted by me.

(d) My friend received me cordially at the time of my reaching there.

Or, After/On reaching/Reaching there, my friend received me cordially.

(e) How excited I was to see the seabeach!

(f) It is larger than any other sea-beach (all other sea-beaches) in the world.

(g) Very few seabeaches in the world are so/as beautiful as it.

(h) We/People call it the pleasure seekers paradise.

(i) Every year a lot of people come here and (they) visit it.

(j) I wish I could visit the seabeach.

Or, Would that I could visit the seabeach.

Explanation:
(a) To make it a complex sentence you need a main clause plus a subordinate clause; for example, add a reason or time: "My friend invited me to pay a visit to Cox’s Bazar because he wanted to show me around." A complex sentence has one independent clause and at least one dependent clause.

(b) Make it negative by placing "not" after the auxiliary verb: "I was not very glad." Negation is formed by adding "not" (or a contraction) to the verb phrase.

(c) Passive: turn the object into the subject and use the appropriate form of "be" + past participle: "The invitation was accepted by me." In passive voice the original object becomes the subject and the doer is optional after "by."

(d) To make it a simple sentence remove the subordinate clause and keep a single independent clause: "My friend received me cordially." A simple sentence has one independent clause only.

(e) Exclamatory: express strong feeling with "How" or an exclamation mark: "How excited I was to see the sea-beach!" Exclamatory sentences show strong emotion and often begin with "What/How" or end with an exclamation mark.

(f) Comparative: compare two things using "more/er ... than": e.g., "It is larger than any other sea-beach nearby." Comparative degree uses "more" or "-er" plus "than" to show comparison between two items.

(g) Positive: use the base adjective without comparison or superlative: "It is beautiful." The positive degree simply states the quality without comparing it to others.

(h) Active: make the agent the subject and use an active verb: "People call it the pleasure seekers’ paradise." In active voice the subject performs the action directly.

(i) Compound: join two independent clauses with a coordinating conjunction: "Every year a lot of people come to visit it, and they enjoy the beach." A compound sentence has two (or more) independent clauses joined by and, but, or, etc.

(j) Active: the sentence is already active because the subject "I" is the doer of "visit" (expressing a wish): "If I could visit the sea-beach!" Active voice has the subject performing the action.

Question #340 (ID: 481339)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Rajshahi Board | Tags: Rajshahi Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) A flower is a glowing gift of nature.(Interrogative)

(b) Isn’t it the symbol of love and beauty?(Affirmative)

(c) Flowers are used on different occasions.(Active)

(d) We present flower to our nearest and dearest person.(Passive)

(e) We need flowers to decorate a place.(Complex)

(f) The rose is the best of all flowers.(Positive)

(g) Having sweet scent and beauty we love it very much.(Compound)

(h) It is lovelier than all other flowers.(Superlative)

(i) The rose is a very nice flower.(Exclamatory)

(j) As the demand for flowers is increasing day by day we should cultivate flower on commercial basis.(Simple)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Isn't a flower a glowing gift of nature?

(b) It is the symbol of love and beauty.

(c) People/We use flowers on different occasions.

(d) Flower is presented to our nearest and dearest persons by us.

(e) We need flowers so that we can decorate a place..

(f) No other flower is as/so good as the rose.

(g) It has sweet scent and beauty and so we love it very much.

(h) It is the loveliest of all flowers.

or, It is the loveliest flower.

(i) What a nice flower the rose is!

(j) Because of the increasing demand for flowers day by day, we should cultivate flower on commercial basis.

Explanation:
(a) To make it interrogative you invert the auxiliary and subject; since the verb is [math]is[/math], ask: "Is a flower a glowing gift of nature?" This makes it a question.

(b) Change the negative question to a positive statement by removing the negative contraction and the question mark: "It is the symbol of love and beauty." This makes it affirmative.

(c) The sentence is passive ("are used"); to make it active, put the doer as the subject and change the verb: "People use flowers on different occasions." Passive agent becomes the subject in active voice.

(d) To form the passive from the active, make the object the subject and use the appropriate form of "to be" + past participle: "Flowers are presented to our nearest and dearest person (by us)." This shows passive construction.

(e) To make it complex, add a subordinate clause (reason/purpose) with a subordinating conjunction: "Because we want to decorate a place, we need flowers." A complex sentence has an independent clause plus a dependent clause.

(f) "The rose is the best of all flowers" is superlative; the positive degree removes comparison: "The rose is good" or "The rose is a beautiful flower." Positive degree uses the base adjective without comparative/superlative markers.

(g) Turn the participial phrase into a separate independent clause and join with a coordinating conjunction to make a compound sentence: "The flower has a sweet scent and beauty, and we love it very much." A compound sentence connects two independent clauses.

(h) Change the comparative phrase into the superlative by using "the" + superlative form: "It is the loveliest of all flowers." Superlative shows the highest degree among all.

(i) Use an exclamatory structure with "What" or "How": "What a very nice flower the rose is!" This expresses strong feeling, so it becomes exclamatory.

(j) To make it simple, keep a single independent clause and remove the subordinating element: "We should cultivate flowers on a commercial basis." A simple sentence has only one independent clause.

Question #341 (ID: 481340)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Barisal Board | Tags: Barisal Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Haji Mohammad Muhsin was not an unkind man at all. (Affirmative)

(b) He inherited vast proerty from his father and sister. (Interrogative)

(c) He was unmarried. (Negative)

(d) During his lifetime, he spent money lavishly to help the poor. (Complex)

(e) One night when he was saying his prayer, a thief broke into his room. (Simple)

(f) Seeing Muhsin the thief cried. (compound)

(g) The thief was caught. (Active)

(h) How needy the thief was! (Assertive)

(i) He gave the thief some food and money. (Passive)

(j) Muhsin was one of the best philanthropists in the world. (Positive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Haji Mohammad Muhsin was a very kind man.

(b) Didn't he inherit vast property from his father and sister?

(c) He was not married/He did not marry.

(d) When he was alive, he spent money lavishly to help the poor.

Or. It was his lifetime when he spent money lavishly to help the poor room.

(e) One night at the time of saying his prayer, a thief broke into his room.

Or. One night while praying a thief broke into his room.

Or. One night during the time of saying his prayer, a thief broke into his room.

(f) The thief saw Muhsin and cried.

(g) Muhsin/He caught the thief.

(h) The thief was very needy.

(i) Some food and money were given to the thief by him.

Or, The thief was given some food and money by him.

(j) Very few philanthropists in the world were so/as good as Muhsin.

Explanation:
(a) The sentence uses litotes (“not unkind”) but conveys a positive meaning; the clear affirmative form is “Haji Mohammad Muhsin was a kind man.” Affirmative sentences state something positively rather than denying it.

(b) To make it interrogative use the auxiliary + subject + base verb pattern: “Did he inherit vast property from his father and sister?” Interrogative sentences are formed by inversion and end with a question mark.

(c) “He was unmarried” is negative because the prefix “un-” shows negation (not married); you can also write it as “He was not married.” Negative sentences express non-existence or denial.

(d) It’s complex because it has a main clause “he spent money lavishly” plus a subordinate purpose clause “to help the poor” (and a temporal phrase “During his lifetime”). A complex sentence contains one independent clause and at least one dependent clause or phrase.

(e) A simple sentence has one independent clause expressing a single idea; the simple version is “One night a thief broke into his room.” It contains one main verb and one complete thought.

(f) A compound sentence joins two independent clauses of equal weight; e.g. “Muhsin saw the thief, and the thief cried.” Use a coordinating conjunction or semicolon to link the clauses.

(g) Active voice places the doer before the verb; the active form is “Someone caught the thief.” Convert passive to active by making the agent the subject and using the main verb in the appropriate tense.

(h) An assertive (declarative) sentence states a fact; the assertive form is “The thief was very needy.” It simply declares the thief’s condition without exclamation.

(i) Passive voice makes the object the subject: “Some food and money were given to the thief by him.” Form the passive with the correct form of “be” + past participle, and optionally include the agent with “by.”

(j) The sentence praises Muhsin, so it is positive in tone: it affirms a good quality (“one of the best philanthropists in the world”). Positive sentences state affirming information rather than negation.

Question #342 (ID: 481341)

Question:
(a) The students studying regularly can expect a good result.(Make it a complex sentence)

(b) But most of our students are inattentive to their studies.(Make it a negative sentence without changing the meaning)

(c) They waste their valuable time idly.(Use passive voice)

(d) Wasting time is harmful for them.(Make it an interrogative sentence)

(e) By repeating this activity they make a poor result.(Make it a complex sentence)

(f) Who loves them then?(Make it a assertive sentence without changing the original meaning)

(g) They are treated badly even by their family members.(Use active voice)

(h) If a student fails in the examination, he suffers from inferiority complex.(Make simple sentence)

(i) No other student in the class is as bad as a failed student.(Use superlative)

(j) So a student should be aware of studying regularly and attentively so that he can do well in the examination.(Make it a simple sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) The students who study regularly can expect a good result.

(b) But most of our students are not attentive to their studies.

(c) Their valuable time is wasted idly by them.

(d) Isn't wasting time harmful to them?

(e) When as they repeat this activity, they make a poor result.

Or. If they repeat this activity, they will make a poor result.

(f) Everybody hates them then.

Or, Nobody loves them then.

(g) Even their family members treat them badly.

(h) By failing in the examination, a student suffers from inferiority complex.

(i) A failed student is the worst in the class.

(j) So a student should be aware of studying regularly and attentively, to do well in the examination.

Explanation:
(a) "If students study regularly, they can expect a good result."  
Explanation: This is a complex sentence because it has a subordinate clause ("If students study regularly") that conditionally supports the main clause ("they can expect a good result"), showing cause and result.

(b) "Most of our students are not attentive to their studies."  
Explanation: Changing "inattentive" to "not attentive" keeps the original negative meaning while using an explicit negative form.

(c) "Their valuable time is wasted idly by them."  
Explanation: The verb phrase is made passive ("is wasted"), moving the focus from the doer to the object ("their valuable time"); the agent "by them" shows who causes it.

(d) "Is wasting time harmful for them?"  
Explanation: To form the question, the auxiliary "is" is placed before the subject phrase "wasting time," turning the statement into an interrogative.

(e) "If they repeat this activity, they will make poor results."  
Explanation: This is a complex sentence: the conditional subordinate clause ("If they repeat this activity") leads to the main clause expressing the consequence ("they will make poor results"), showing cause and effect. (You can also say "they will get poor results" for more natural wording.)

(f) "No one loves them then."  
Explanation: The interrogative "Who loves them then?" implies a negative answer; converting it to an assertive sentence uses "No one" to state that directly while preserving meaning.

(g) "Even their family members treat them badly."  
Explanation: Active voice makes the agent ("their family members") the subject performing the action ("treat them badly"), which reverses the original passive structure.

(h) "A failed student suffers from an inferiority complex."  
Explanation: This simple sentence condenses the conditional idea into a single statement by using "failed" as an adjective describing the student.

(i) "A failed student is the worst in the class."  
Explanation: The comparative idea ("No other student ... is as bad") is changed to a superlative form ("the worst") to show that the failed student ranks lowest among all students.

(j) "A student should study regularly and attentively to do well in the examination."  
Explanation: The complex original is simplified by combining purpose into an infinitive phrase ("to do well"), making one clear simple sentence that states duty and result.

Question #343 (ID: 481342)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards: Dinajpur Board | Tags: Dinajpur Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Madhusudan Dutt was a very popular poet. (Make it an exclamatory sentence)

(b) He was one of the greatest dramatists in Bangla literature. (Make it positive degree)

(c) He was born at Sagordari on the bank of the Kapotaksho. (Make it a complex sentence)

(d) When he was a boy, he desired to be an Englishman. (Make it a simple sentence)

(e) He was recognised by his teachers as a precious child. (Make it an active voice)

(f) He thought that he was born on the wrong side of the planet. (Make it an interrogative sentence)

(g) He also thought that his society was unable to appreciate his intellect. (Make it a negative sentence)

(h) Again he believed that none but the West would be more receptive to his creative genius. (Make it an affirmative sentence)

(i) He was an ardent follower of Lord Byron. (Make it an interrogative sentence)

(j) He went to Europe and started composing poems. (Make it a simple sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) What a popular poet Madhusudan Dutt was!

(b) Very few dramatists in Bangla literature were as/so great as he.

(c) He was born at Sagordart which is/stands on the bank of the Kapotaksho.

(d) In/At/From his boyhood, he desired to be an Englishman.

(e) His teachers recognized him as a precious child.

(f) Didn't he think that he was born on the wrong side of the planet?

(g) He also thought that his society was not able to appreciate his intellect.

(h) Again he believed that only the West would be more receptive to his creative genius.

(i) Wasn't he an ardent follower of Lord Byron?

(j) Going to Europe, he started composing poems.

Explanation:
(a) What a popular poet Madhusudan Dutt was!  
This is exclamatory: "What" + noun phrase + subject + verb expresses strong feeling.

(b) He was a great dramatist in Bangla literature.  
Positive degree uses the base adjective "great" instead of the superlative/comparative phrase "one of the greatest."

(c) He was born at Sagordari, which lies on the bank of the Kapotaksho.  
This is a complex sentence because it has an independent clause ("He was born at Sagordari") plus a dependent relative clause ("which lies on the bank of the Kapotaksho") that adds extra information.

(d) As a boy he desired to be an Englishman.  
A simple sentence with one independent clause stating the subject, time phrase, and action.

(e) His teachers recognised him as a precious child.  
Active voice: the doer ("his teachers") is the subject and performs the verb "recognised" on the object "him."

(f) Did he think that he was born on the wrong side of the planet?  
Formed as an interrogative by using the auxiliary "did" for past tense and placing it before the subject.

(g) He also thought that his society did not appreciate his intellect.  
Negative sentence: "did not" negates the verb "appreciate," conveying the same idea as "was unable to appreciate."

(h) Again he believed that only the West would be more receptive to his creative genius.  
Affirmative form replaces the negative phrase "none but" with the positive word "only."

(i) Was he an ardent follower of Lord Byron?  
Interrogative formed by inverting the auxiliary "was" and the subject "he."

(j) He went to Europe and began composing poems.  
A simple sentence with one subject doing two actions (compound predicate) within a single independent clause.

Question #344 (ID: 481343)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Haji Muhammad Muhsin was more generous than many other men in this subcontinent. (Use positive degree)

(b) He was born in Hoogly. (Make it a complex sentence)

(c) He inherited a vast property from his father and sister. (Make it an interrogative sentence)

(d) He did not misuse this wealth. (Use passive voice)

(e) He is called the friend of humanity. (Use active voice)

(f) He did not marry. (Make it an affirmative sentence)

(g) During his lifetime he spent money lavishly to help the poor. (Make it a complex sentence)

(h) He was so kind that he could not refuse any one's request. (Make it a compound sentence)

(i) One night when he was saying his prayer a thief broke into his room. (Make it a simple sentence)

(j) He caught the thief but did not punish him. (Make it a complex sentence)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Very few men in this subcontinent were so/as generous as Haji Muhammad Muhsin.

(b) It is Hoogly where he was born. / Hoogly is the place where he was born.

(c) Didn't he inherit a vast property from his father and sister?

Or. Did he not (Or, Didn't he) inherit a vast property from his father and sister?

(d) This wealth was not misused by him.

(e) People/We call him the friend of humanity.

(f) He was unmarried.

Or, He was a bachelor.

(g) When he lived, he spent money lavishly to help the poor.

Or, When he was alive, he spent money lavishly to help the poor.

(h) He was very kind and so he could not refuse any one's request.

(i) One night at the time of his saying prayer, a thief broke into his room.

Or. One night while saying his prayer, a thief broke into his room.

(j) Though/Although he caught the thief, he did not punish him.

Explanation:
(a) Answer: Haji Muhammad Muhsin was generous.
Explanation: "More generous" is comparative; the positive degree uses the base adjective "generous" without comparison.

(b) Answer: He was born in Hoogly, where he spent his early years.
Explanation: This is complex because it has one main clause ("He was born in Hoogly") and one dependent relative clause ("where he spent his early years") that cannot stand alone.

(c) Answer: Did he inherit a vast property from his father and sister?
Explanation: Past simple questions are formed by adding the auxiliary "did" and using the base form of the verb ("inherit"), with subject–auxiliary inversion.

(d) Answer: This wealth was not misused by him.
Explanation: Passive voice makes the object ("this wealth") the subject and uses a form of "be" + past participle ("was ... misused"); the agent can be added with "by ...".

(e) Answer: People call him the friend of humanity.
Explanation: Active voice names the doer ("People") as the subject and the person acted on ("him") as the object, using a simple present active verb ("call").

(f) Answer: He remained a bachelor.
Explanation: This is an affirmative statement of the same fact; it reports his marital status without using negation.

(g) Answer: While he was alive, he spent money lavishly to help the poor.
Explanation: This is a complex sentence because it begins with a subordinate adverbial clause ("While he was alive") followed by the main clause describing his spending.

(h) Answer: He was kind, and he could not refuse anyone's request.
Explanation: This is a compound sentence: two independent clauses ("He was kind" and "he could not refuse anyone's request") joined by the coordinating conjunction "and."

(i) Answer: One night a thief broke into his room during his prayer.
Explanation: This is a simple sentence with a single independent clause; "during his prayer" is a prepositional phrase, not a subordinate clause.

(j) Answer: Although he caught the thief, he did not punish him.
Explanation: This is complex because it uses a subordinate concessive clause ("Although he caught the thief") plus a main clause ("he did not punish him"), showing contrast.

Question #345 (ID: 481344)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2015 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Health is wealth. (Make complex sentence)

(b) A healthy poor man is happier than a sick moneyed man. (Use positive degree)

(c) Though a healthy man is an asset to his family, an unhealthy man is a liability. (Make compound sentence)

(d) He can succeed in life. (Make interrogative sentence)

(e) So, everybody cannot but be conscious of his health. (Make affirmative sentence)

(f) Everybody must take care of his health all the time. (Make negative sentence)

(g) Health can be improved by regular physical exercise and a balanced diet. (Use active voice)

(h) The people who are poor cannot afford to take a balanced diet. (Make simple sentence)

(i) They are very concerned with the quantity of food. (Make exclamatory)

(j) Everybody should know it that malnutrition causes weakness. (Use passive voice)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) It is health which is wealth.

(b) A sick moneyed man is not as/so happy as a healthy poor man.

(c) A healthy man is an asset to his family but an unhealthy man is a liability.

(d) Can't he succeed in life?

(e) So, everybody must be conscious of his health.

(f) Everybody cannot but take care of his health all the time.

(g) Regular physical exercise and a balanced diet can improve health.

(h) The poor people cannot afford to take a balanced diet.

Or. The people being poor can't afford to take a balanced diet.

(i) How concerned they are with the quantity of food!

Or. How concerned with the quantity of food they are!

(j) It should be known to everybody that weakness is caused by malnutrition.

Explanation:
(a) Since health is wealth, one should take care of it.
Explanation: This is a complex sentence because it has a main clause and a subordinate clause introduced by "since," which shows reason.

(b) A sick moneyed man is not as happy as a healthy poor man.
Explanation: The comparative "happier than" is changed to the positive-degree form "not as ... as," keeping the same meaning while using the base adjective "happy."

(c) A healthy man is an asset to his family, but an unhealthy man is a liability.
Explanation: Two independent clauses are joined by the coordinating conjunction "but," making a compound sentence.

(d) Can he succeed in life?
Explanation: Forming an interrogative with a modal verb requires inverting the subject and the auxiliary: "can" + subject + main verb.

(e) So, everybody must be conscious of his health.
Explanation: "Cannot but be" means "must be," so the affirmative form uses "must" + adjective to express the same idea.

(f) Everybody must not neglect to take care of his health all the time.
Explanation: This negative sentence uses "must not neglect to..." to express the required obligation in a negated form while preserving the original meaning.

(g) Regular physical exercise and a balanced diet can improve health.
Explanation: Convert the passive "Health can be improved by..." into active voice by making the agents the subject and the action active.

(h) Poor people cannot afford a balanced diet.
Explanation: The relative clause "who are poor" is reduced to the simple noun phrase "poor people," forming a simple sentence with one subject and one predicate.

(i) How concerned they are with the quantity of food!
Explanation: An exclamatory sentence is formed with "How" plus adjective and subject to express strong feeling.

(j) It should be known by everybody that weakness is caused by malnutrition.
Explanation: "Everybody should know" is changed to passive "It should be known by everybody," and "malnutrition causes weakness" is converted to the passive "weakness is caused by malnutrition."

Question #346 (ID: 481345)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2010 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Computer is one of the greatest inventions of modern science. (Positive) (b) Computer is a blessing on earth. (Negative) (c) Though it is a blessing, it has dark sides. (Simple) (d) Computers are nowadays being used in almost every sphere of life. (Active) (e) We cannot but depend on it. (Affirmative) (f) No one can deny its necessity. (Interrogative) (g) It is the most used device in our life. (Comparative) (h) It helps us a lot. (Passive) (i) Because of its usefulness, it has become very popular. (Compound) (j) Without computer, we cannot imagine our modern life. (Complex)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) Correct: Positive (affirmative declarative). This sentence praises the computer and states a fact without any negation, so it is positive and declarative.  

(b) Correct classification is Positive, not Negative. The sentence expresses a favourable view (“a blessing”) and contains no negation, so it is positive.  

(c) Correct: Complex. The subordinating conjunction "Though" introduces a subordinate clause, so the sentence has a dependent clause plus a main clause, making it complex.  

(d) Correct: Passive. The verb phrase "are being used" is passive voice (the action is received by "computers"), not active.  

(e) Correct as Affirmative in meaning. Although it contains "cannot," the idiom "cannot but depend" means "must depend" (an affirmative meaning), so its force is affirmative.  

(f) Correct classification is Negative (declarative), not Interrogative. "No one" negates the sentence, so it is a negative declarative statement.  

(g) Correct: Superlative, not comparative. The word "most" shows the highest degree (superlative), whereas comparative would use "more."  

(h) Correct: Active. The subject "It" performs the action "helps," so the sentence is in active voice, not passive.  

(i) Correct: Simple (not compound). The sentence has a single independent clause with an adverbial phrase "Because of its usefulness," so it is a simple sentence.  

(j) Correct: Simple (not complex). "Without computer" is an introductory prepositional phrase and the rest is one independent clause, so the whole sentence is a simple declarative sentence.

Question #347 (ID: 481346)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2010 | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
(a) Terrorism is a devastating phenomenon of the modern world. (Exclamatory) (b) At present, it is increasing alarmingly. (Interrogative) (c) Nothing is as disastrous as terrorism. (Comparative) (d) It is one of the most corrosive problems of the modern world. (Positive) (e) A terrorist is hated by people. (Active) (f) Who is not now in the threat of violence? (Assertive) (g) Though there are laws to punish the terrorists, they are not properly applied. (Compound) (h) By applying the laws properly, we can get rid of terrorism. (Complex) (i) What a miserable life a terrorist leads! (Assertive) (j) They should be brought to book. (Active)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:


Explanation:
(a) Correct: Exclamatory. Reason: The sentence expresses strong feeling and would normally end with an exclamation mark, which makes it exclamatory.

(b) Correct label: Declarative (Assertive), not Interrogative. Reason: It states a fact and ends with a full stop, so it is a statement, not a question.

(c) Correct: Comparative. Reason: The structure "as … as" compares two things, showing degree of comparison.

(d) Correct label: Superlative, not Positive. Reason: "one of the most corrosive" uses "most," indicating the highest degree among a group.

(e) Correct label: Passive, not Active. Reason: The subject ("A terrorist") receives the action ("is hated"); the active form would be "People hate a terrorist."

(f) Correct: Interrogative, not Assertive. Reason: It asks a question beginning with "Who," so it is an interrogative sentence.

(g) Correct: Complex, not Compound. Reason: It has a subordinate clause introduced by "Though" plus a main clause, so one dependent and one independent clause (complex).

(h) Correct label: Simple (Declarative), not Complex. Reason: There is a single main clause with a participial phrase ("By applying…")—so it is a simple declarative sentence.

(i) Correct: Exclamatory, not Assertive. Reason: "What a miserable life…!" expresses strong feeling and is an exclamation.

(j) Correct label: Passive, not Active. Reason: The verb phrase "should be brought" is passive (the subject receives the action).

Question #348 (ID: 481347)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Jessore Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Read the text and change the sentences as directed in the brackets:

(a) I am sure that man is the maker of his own fortune. (Negative)

(b) A man has to make a proper use of his time to shine in life. (Imperative)

(c) Who doesn't know it. (Passive voice)

(d) The lazy suffer miserably in the long run. (Exclamatory)

(e) To kill time is as harmful as to commit suicide. (Comparative)

(f) Our life is only a sum total of hours, days and years. (Negative)

(g) Youth is the most valuable season of life. (Positive)

(h) In youth, our mind can be shaped easily. (Active voice)

(i) We should utilize our time properly in youth. (Imperative)

(j) It is called the seedtime of life. (Active voice)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Changing Sentences:

(a) I am not doubtful that man is the maker of his own fortune. (আমার সন্দেহ নেই যে মানুষ নিজেই তার ভাগ্যের নির্মাতা।)

(b) Let a man make a proper use of his time to shine in life. (জীবনে উন্নতি করতে মানুষকে সময়ের যথাযথ ব্যবহার করতে দাও।)'

(c) To whom is it not known? (কার কাছে এটা জানা নেই?/কার কাছে এটি অজানা?)

(d) How miserably the lazy suffer in the long run! (পরিণামে অলসরা কতই না চরম কষ্ট ভোগ করে!) (e) To commit suicide is not more harmful than to kill time. (আত্মহত্যা করা সময় নষ্ট করার চেয়ে বেশি ক্ষতিকর নয়।)

(f) Our life is nothing but a sum total of hours, days and years. (আমাদের জীবন ঘন্টা, দিন এবং বছরের সমষ্টি ছাড়া আর কিছুই নয়।)

(g) No other season of life is as valuable as youth. (জীবনের অন্য কোনো সময় যৌবনকালের মত অতটা মূল্যবান নয়।) (h) In youth, we can shape our mind easily. (যৌবনে আমরা আমাদের মনকে সহজেই গঠন করতে পারি।)

(i) Let us utilize our time properly in youth. (চলো-যৌবনে আমরা সময়কে সঠিকভাবে কাজে লাগাই।)

(j) People call it the seedtime of life. (লোকেরা একে জীবনের বীজ বপনের সময় বলে।)

Explanation:
(a) I am not sure that man is the maker of his own fortune.
Explanation: Negation is formed by inserting "not" after the auxiliary "am," which turns the affirmative certainty into its negative form.

(b) Use your time properly to shine in life.
Explanation: An imperative gives a direct command; here the verb "use" is in the base form addressing the reader to make the sentence imperative.

(c) By whom is it not known?
Explanation: To make the question passive, the object ("it") becomes the subject and the agent is expressed with "by," changing the structure while keeping the meaning.

(d) How miserably the lazy suffer in the long run!
Explanation: Exclamatory sentences often begin with "How" or "What" to emphasize feeling; here "How miserably..." expresses strong emotion about their suffering.

(e) Killing time is as harmful as committing suicide.
Explanation: Use of gerunds ("killing," "committing") and the structure "as ... as" makes a comparative of equality, showing two actions are equally harmful.

(f) Our life is not only a sum total of hours, days and years.
Explanation: Changing "only" to "not only" makes the sentence negative while implying there is more to life than just its measurable parts.

(g) Youth is a valuable season of life.
Explanation: Converting the superlative "most valuable" to the positive degree uses the base adjective "valuable," stating the quality without comparison.

(h) We can easily shape our minds in youth.
Explanation: Active voice makes the doer ("we") the subject and uses the verb "shape" directly; adverb placement "easily" modifies the verb.

(i) Utilize your time properly in youth.
Explanation: The imperative form uses the base verb "utilize" (or "use") to give a direct instruction to the reader.

(j) People call it the seedtime of life.
Explanation: To change from passive ("it is called") to active, introduce a subject ("People") who perform the action and use the verb "call."

Question #349 (ID: 481348)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years: 2023 | Boards:  | Tags: Cumilla Board
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as diredted in brackets:

(a) We are grateful to the freedom fighters. (Negative)

(b) Their contribution is greater than any other thing. (Superlative)

(c) You should never disrespect or forget our martyrs. (Imperative)

(d) The national memorial has been built with a view to paying tribute to their memories. (Active)

e) A freedom fighter is the greatest son of the soil. (Comparative)

( (f) We gotsour independence for their sacrifice. (Passive)

(g) They fought very bravely to snatch the red sun of independence. (Exclamatory)

(h) Their courage was more powerful than their weapons. (Positive)

(i) Their contribution will never be forgotten. (Active)

(j) The government has taken some steps to improve their condition. (Passive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Changing Sentences:

(a) We are not ungrateful to the freedom fighters. (মুক্তিযোদ্ধাদের প্রতি আমরা অকৃতজ্ঞ নই।)

(b) Their contribution is the greatest thing. (তাদের অবদান সবচেয়ে বড় জিনিস।)

(c) Never disrespect or forget our martyrs. (আমাদের শহিদদের কখনো অসম্মান করবে না বা ভুলে যাবে না।)

(d) The govt. has built the national memorial with a view to paying tribute to their memories. (সরকার তাদের স্মৃতির প্রতি শ্রদ্ধা জানাতে জাতীয় স্মৃতিসৌধ নির্মাণ করেছে।)

(e) A freedom fighter is greater than any other son of the soil. (একজন মুক্তিযোদ্ধা দেশের যে কোনো সন্তানের চেয়ে বড়।)

(f) Our independence was got by us for their sacrifice. (তাদের আত্মত্যাগের বিনিময়ে আমাদের স্বাধীনতা অর্জিত হয়েছিল।)

(g) How bravely they fought to snatch the red sun of independence! (স্বাধীনতার লাল সূর্য ছিনিয়ে আনতে তারা কতই না সাহসের সাথে যুদ্ধ করেছিল।)

(h) Their weapons were not so powerful as their courage. (তাদের অস্ত্র তাদের সাহসের মত অতটা শক্তিশালী ছিল না।)

(i) We will never forget their contribution. (আমরা তাদের অবদান কখনই ভুলব না।)

(j) Some steps have been taken to improve their condition by the government. (তাদের অবস্থার উন্নতির জন্য সরকার কর্তৃক কিছু পদক্ষেপ গ্রহণ করা হয়েছে।)

Explanation:
(a) "We are not ungrateful to the freedom fighters."  
Explanation: Negation is formed by adding "not" or using the negative adjective "ungrateful"; here "are not ungrateful" expresses the negative of "are grateful."

(b) "Their contribution is the greatest."  
Explanation: Superlative degree uses "the" + adjective + "-est" (or "most"); "greatest" shows their contribution is highest among all.

(c) "Never disrespect or forget our martyrs."  
Explanation: Imperative sentences give commands and drop the subject "you"; the verbs start in base form ("disrespect", "forget") and "never" makes it a negative command.

(d) "They have built the national memorial to pay tribute to their memories."  
Explanation: To change passive to active, introduce the agent ("they") and use an active verb form ("have built") instead of "has been built."

(e) "A freedom fighter is greater than any other son of the soil."  
Explanation: Comparative degree compares two or more items using "greater than"; it replaces the superlative "greatest" with a comparative structure.

(f) "Our independence was won because of their sacrifice."  
Explanation: Passive form emphasizes the object ("our independence") by making it the subject and using a past passive verb phrase ("was won") while the agent may be omitted.

(g) "How bravely they fought to snatch the red sun of independence!"  
Explanation: Exclamatory sentences use "How" (with adverb) or "What" (with noun) + subject + verb to express strong feeling.

(h) "Their courage was powerful."  
Explanation: To put the sentence in the positive degree, remove the comparative "more ... than" and use the base adjective "powerful."

(i) "We will never forget their contribution."  
Explanation: Change passive ("will never be forgotten") to active by adding an agent ("we") and using an active verb ("will never forget").

(j) "Some steps have been taken by the government to improve their condition."  
Explanation: Passive is formed by making the object ("some steps") the subject and using the appropriate form of "be" + past participle ("have been taken"), with the agent added after "by."
